             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Operation_Una" title="Operation Una">
               Una
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="/wiki/Operation_Southern_Move" title="Operation Southern Move">
               Southern Move
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        </a>
        Stone at
        <a href="/wiki/Donji_Poto%C4%8Dari" title="Donji Potoari">
         Potoari
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_2005_burial.jpg">

        Burial of 610 identified Bosniaks in 2005
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica2007.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Srebrenica2007.jpg/220px-Srebrenica2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Srebrenica2007.jpg/330px-Srebrenica2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Srebrenica2007.jpg/440px-Srebrenica2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">

        Burial of 465 identified Bosniaks in 2007
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20114124.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="720" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/20114124.jpg/220px-20114124.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/20114124.jpg/330px-20114124.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/20114124.jpg/440px-20114124.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20114124.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Burial of 775 identified victims in 2010
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <b>
       Srebrenica massacre
      </b>
      , also known as the
      <b>
       Srebrenica genocide
      </b>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IWPR_Oct31_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IWPR_Oct31-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">
       Bosnian
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="bs" xml:lang="bs">
       <i>
        Genocid u Srebrenici
       </i>
      </span>
      ), was the
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocidal
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      killing, in July 1995, of more than 8,000
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-potocarimc.ba_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-potocarimc.ba-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Muslim
      <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">
       Bosniaks
      </a>
      , mainly men and boys, in and around the town of
      <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
       Srebrenica
      </a>
      during the
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">
       Bosnian War
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The killings were perpetrated by units of the Bosnian Serb
      <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska" title="Army of Republika Srpska">
       Army of Republika Srpska
      </a>
      (VRS)
      <a href="/wiki/Command_responsibility" title="Command responsibility">
       under the command
      </a>
      of General
      <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87" title="Ratko Mladi">
       Ratko Mladi
      </a>
      . The Secretary-General of the United Nations described the
      <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">
       mass murder
      </a>
      as the worst crime on European soil since the Second World War.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_SecGen_10th_anniv_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-UN_SecGen_10th_anniv-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iwpr.net_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-iwpr.net-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A paramilitary unit from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1990%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Serbia (19902006)">
       Serbia
      </a>
      known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Scorpions_(paramilitary)" title="Scorpions (paramilitary)">
       Scorpions
      </a>
      , officially part of the Serbian Interior Ministry until 1991, participated in the massacre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Williams-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 1993, the United Nations declared the besieged
      <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">
       enclave
      </a>
      of Srebrenicain the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drina_Valley" title="Drina Valley">
       Drina Valley
      </a>
      of northeastern
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnia" title="Bosnia">
       Bosnia
      </a>
      a "
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Safe_Areas" title="United Nations Safe Areas">
       safe area
      </a>
      " under UN protection. However, in July 1995,
      <a href="/wiki/Dutchbat" title="Dutchbat">
       UNPROFOR Dutchbat
      </a>
      's
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      370
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      soldiers in Srebrenica failed
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to prevent the town's capture by the VRSand the subsequent massacre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.vandiepen.com_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-www.vandiepen.com-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The "Dutchbat", originating from a seperate Dutch military unit, was subordinate to a Norwegian Brigadier General and a French General.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2004, in a unanimous ruling on the case of
      <i>
       Prosecutor v. Krsti
      </i>
      , the Appeals Chamber of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
       International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia
      </a>
      (ICTY), located in
      <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">
       the Hague
      </a>
      , ruled that the massacre of the enclave's male inhabitants constituted
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      , a crime under international law.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ruling was also upheld by the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </a>
      (ICJ) in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The forcible transfer of between 25,000 and 30,000 Bosniak women, children and elderly which accompanied the massacre was found to be confirming evidence of the genocidal intent of members of the VRS Main Staff who orchestrated the massacre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005, in a message to the tenth anniversary commemoration of the massacre, the Secretary-General of the United Nations noted that, while blame lay first and foremost with those who planned and carried out the massacre and those who assisted and harboured them, the powers with the ability to respond had failed to respond adequately; some taunted that the UN itself made serious errors of judgement, qualifying the tragedy of Srebrenica as an event that would forever haunt the history of the UN.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_SecGen_10th_anniv_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-UN_SecGen_10th_anniv-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Meanwhile, in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Genocide_case" title="Bosnian Genocide case">
        Bosnian Genocide case
       </a>
      </i>
      before the International Court of Justice,
      <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">
       Serbia and Montenegro
      </a>
      was cleared of direct responsibility for, or complicity in, the massacre, but was found responsible for not doing enough to prevent the genocide and not prosecuting those responsible, in breach of the
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Convention" title="Genocide Convention">
       Genocide Convention
      </a>
      . The
      <i>
       Preliminary List of People Missing or Killed in Srebrenica
      </i>
      compiled by the Bosnian Federal Commission of Missing Persons contains 8,373 names.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-potocarimc.ba_1-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-potocarimc.ba-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of July 2012, 6,838 genocide victims have been identified through DNA analysis of body parts recovered from mass graves;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as of July 2013, 6,066 victims have been buried at the
      <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica_Genocide_Memorial" title="Srebrenica Genocide Memorial">
       Memorial Centre of Potoari
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In April 2013, Serbian
      <a href="/wiki/President_of_Serbia" title="President of Serbia">
       President
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikoli">
       Tomislav Nikoli
      </a>
      officially apologized for the massacre, although he stopped short of calling it genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 8, 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      vetoed, by request of the
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      and Serbia, a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_resolution" title="UN resolution">
       UN resolution
      </a>
      condemning the Srebrenica massacre as genocide, branding the resolution as "anti-Serb".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 9, 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
       Members of the European Parliament (EP)
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       House of Representatives of the U.S. Congress
      </a>
      unanimously adopted its resolution on Srebrenica defining the crime as genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

           </span>
          </a>
          <ul>
           <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8">
            <a href="#April_1993:_the_Security_Council_declares_Srebrenica_a_.22safe_area.22">
             <span class="tocnumber">

             </span>
             <span class="toctext">

             </span>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9">

             </span>

             </span>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10">

             <span class="toctext">

           </li>
           <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11">

             <span class="tocnumber">

             <span class="toctext">

         </li>

       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">
        <a href="#Massacre">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          2
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          Massacre
         </span>
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">
          <a href="#11.E2.80.9313_July_1995:_the_increasing_concentration_of_refugees_in_Poto.C4.8Dari">

      </ul>
     </div>
     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Background">
       Background
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict_in_eastern_Bosnia">
       Conflict in eastern Bosnia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conflict in eastern Bosnia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">
       Yugoslav Wars
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_War" title="Bosnian War">
       Bosnian War
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The multiethnic
      <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Socialist Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       Socialist Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      was mainly inhabited by Muslim
      <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">
       Bosniaks
      </a>
      (44 percent),
      <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
       Serbs
      </a>
      (31 percent) and Catholic
      <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">
       Croats
      </a>
      (17 percent). Following a declaration of national sovereignty on 15 October 1991 as the former Yugoslavia began to disintegrate, a
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="History of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       referendum for independence
      </a>
      was held on 29 February 1992. The result, in favour of independence, was rejected by the political representatives of the Bosnian Serbs who had boycotted the referendum. The
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      was formally recognised by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">
       European Community
      </a>
      on 6 April 1992, and by the United States the following day. Following the declaration of independence, Bosnian Serb forces, supported by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_government" title="Serbian government">
       Serbian government
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Miloevi">
       Slobodan Miloevi
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_People%27s_Army" title="Yugoslav People's Army">
       Yugoslav People's Army
      </a>
      (JNA), attacked the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina in order to unify and secure Serb territory. A fierce struggle for territorial control ensued, accompanied by the ethnic cleansing of the non-Serb population from areas under Serb control; in particular, the Bosniak population of Eastern Bosnia, near the border with Serbia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Kunarac.2C_Kova.C4.8D_and_Vukovi.C4.87_judgement_.E2.80.93_Fo.C4.8Da_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Kunarac.2C_Kova.C4.8D_and_Vukovi.C4.87_judgement_.E2.80.93_Fo.C4.8Da-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1992_ethnic_cleansing_campaign">
       1992 ethnic cleansing campaign
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1992 ethnic cleansing campaign">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The predominantly Bosniak area of Central
      <a href="/wiki/Podrinje" title="Podrinje">
       Podrinje
      </a>
      (the region around Srebrenica) had a primary strategic importance to Serbs, as without it there would be no territorial integrity within their new political entity of
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They thus proceeded with the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">
       ethnic cleansing
      </a>
      of Bosniaks from Bosniak ethnic territories in Eastern Bosnia and Central Podrinje. In the words of the ICTY judgement:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Once towns and villages were securely in their hands, the Serb forces  the military, the police, the paramilitaries and, sometimes, even Serb villagers  applied the same pattern: Muslim houses and apartments were systematically ransacked or burnt down, Muslim villagers were rounded up or captured and, in the process, sometimes beaten or killed. Men and women were separated, with many of the men detained in the former KP Dom prison.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Kunarac.2C_Kova.C4.8D_and_Vukovi.C4.87_judgement_.E2.80.93_Fo.C4.8Da_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Kunarac.2C_Kova.C4.8D_and_Vukovi.C4.87_judgement_.E2.80.93_Fo.C4.8Da-39">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         39
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      In neighbouring
      <a href="/wiki/Bratunac" title="Bratunac">
       Bratunac
      </a>
      , Bosniaks were either killed or forced to flee to Srebrenica, resulting in 1,156 deaths, according to Bosnian government data.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bratunac_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bratunac-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Thousands of Bosniaks were also killed in
      <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da_massacres" title="Foa massacres">
       Foa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zvornik" title="Zvornik">
       Zvornik
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cerska" title="Cerska">
       Cerska
      </a>
      and Snagovo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IDC:_Podrinje_victim_statistics_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IDC:_Podrinje_victim_statistics-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Fate_of_Bosniak_villages">
       Fate of Bosniak villages
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Fate of Bosniak villages">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The Bosnian Institute in the UK has published a list of 296 villages destroyed by Serb forces around Srebrenica during the first three months of war (April  June 1992):
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       More than three years before the 1995 Srebrenica genocide, Bosnian Serb nationalists  with the logistical, moral and financial support of Serbia and the Yugoslav People's Army (JNA)  destroyed 296 predominantly Bosniak villages in the region around Srebrenica, forcibly uprooting some 70,000 Bosniaks from their homes and systematically massacring at least 3,166 Bosniaks (documented deaths) including many women, children and elderly.
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      According to the
      <a href="/wiki/Naser_Ori%C4%87" title="Naser Ori">
       Naser Ori
      </a>
      trial judgement:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Between April 1992 and March 1993, the town of Srebrenica and the villages in the area held by Bosniak were constantly subjected to Serb military assaults, including artillery attacks, sniper fire, as well as occasional bombing from aircraft. Each onslaught followed a similar pattern. Serb soldiers and paramilitaries surrounded a Bosnian Muslim village or hamlet, called upon the population to surrender their weapons, and then began with indiscriminate shelling and shooting. In most cases, they then entered the village or hamlet, expelled or killed the population, who offered no significant resistance, and destroyed their homes. During this period, Srebrenica was subjected to indiscriminate shelling from all directions on a daily basis. Potoari in particular was a daily target for Serb artillery and infantry because it was a sensitive point in the defence line around Srebrenica. Other Bosnian Muslim settlements were routinely attacked as well. All this resulted in a great number of refugees and casualties.
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_for_Srebrenica_1992.E2.80.931993">
       Struggle for Srebrenica 19921993
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Struggle for Srebrenica 19921993">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Serb military and paramilitary forces from the area and neighbouring parts of eastern Bosnia and Serbia gained control of Srebrenica for several weeks in early 1992, killing and expelling Bosniak civilians. In May 1992, Bosnian government forces under the leadership of Ori recaptured the town.
     </p>
     <p>
      Over the remainder of 1992, offensives by Bosnian government forces from Srebrenica increased the area under their control, and by January 1993 they had linked with Bosniak-held
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDepa" title="epa">
       epa
      </a>
      to the south and Cerska to the west. At this time, the Srebrenica enclave had reached its peak size of 900 square kilometres (350 sq miles), although it was never linked to the main area of Bosnian-government controlled land in the west and remained, in the words of the ICTY, "a vulnerable island amid Serb-controlled territory".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Over the next few months, the Serb military captured the villages of Konjevi Polje and Cerska, severing the link between Srebrenica and epa and reducing the size of the Srebrenica enclave to 150 square kilometres. Bosniak residents of the outlying areas converged on the town of Srebrenica and its population swelled to between 50,000 and 60,000 people.
     </p>
     <p>
      General
      <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Morillon" title="Philippe Morillon">
       Philippe Morillon
      </a>
      of France, Commander of the United Nations Protection Force (UNPROFOR), visited Srebrenica in March 1993. By then, the town was overcrowded and
      <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">
       siege
      </a>
      conditions prevailed. There was almost no running water as the advancing Serb forces had destroyed the town's water supplies; people relied on makeshift generators for electricity. Food, medicine and other essentials were extremely scarce. Before leaving, General Morillon told the panicked residents of Srebrenica at a public gathering that the town was under the protection of the UN and that he would never abandon them.
     </p>
     <p>
      Between March and April 1993 several thousand Bosniaks were evacuated from Srebrenica under the auspices of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="UN High Commissioner for Refugees">
       UN High Commissioner for Refugees
      </a>
      (UNHCR). The evacuations were opposed by the Bosnian government in
      <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">
       Sarajevo
      </a>
      as contributing to the ethnic cleansing of predominantly Bosniak territory.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Serb authorities remained intent on capturing the enclave. On 13 April 1993, the Serbs told the UNHCR representatives that they would attack the town within two days unless the Bosniaks surrendered and agreed to be evacuated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Bosniaks refused to surrender.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Starvation_in_Srebrenica_1992.E2.80.931995">
       Starvation in Srebrenica 19921995
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Starvation in Srebrenica 19921995">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A former Serb soldier of the "
      <a href="/wiki/JSO_(Special_Operations_Unit)#History" title="JSO (Special Operations Unit)">
       Red Berets
      </a>
      " unit described the tactics used to starve and kill the besieged population of Srebrenica:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       "It was almost like a game, a cat-and-mouse hunt. But of course we greatly outnumbered the Muslims, so in almost all cases, we were the hunters and they were the prey. We needed them to surrender, but how do you get someone to surrender in a war like this? You starve them to death. So very quickly we realized that it wasn't really weapons being smuggled into Srebrenica that we should worry about, but food. They were truly starving in there, so they would send people out to steal cattle or gather crops, and our job was to find and kill them... No prisoners. Well, yes, if we thought they had useful information, we might keep them alive until we got it out of them, but in the end, no prisoners. The local people became quite indignant, so sometimes we would keep someone alive to hand over to them [to kill] just to keep them happy."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-47">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         47
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      When Australian journalist Tony Birtley visited the besieged Srebrenica in March 1993, he took footage of Bosniak civilians starving to death.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Judgment of the Hague Tribunal in the case of Naser Oric found that:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       "Bosnian Serb forces controlling the access roads were not allowing international humanitarian aid  most importantly, food and medicine  to reach Srebrenica. As a consequence, there was a constant and serious shortage of food causing starvation to peak in the winter of 1992/1993. Numerous people died or were in an extremely emaciated state due to malnutrition. Bosnian Muslim fighters and their families, however, were provided with food rations from existing storage facilities. The most disadvantaged group among the Bosnian Muslims were the refugees, who usually lived on the streets and without shelter, in freezing temperatures. Only in November and December 1992, did two UN convoys with humanitarian aid reach the enclave, and this despite Bosnian Serb obstruction."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         49
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Srebrenica_.22safe_area.22">
       The Srebrenica "safe area"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title='Edit section: The Srebrenica "safe area"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="657" data-file-width="660" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg/220px-Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg/330px-Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg/440px-Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bosnia_areas_of_control_Sep_94.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Areas of control in Bosnia and Herzegovina in September 1994; eastern Bosnian enclaves near the Serbian border
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="April_1993:_the_Security_Council_declares_Srebrenica_a_.22safe_area.22">
       April 1993: the Security Council declares Srebrenica a "safe area"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title='Edit section: April 1993: the Security Council declares Srebrenica a "safe area"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 16 April 1993, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">
       United Nations Security Council
      </a>
      passed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resolution_819" title="Resolution 819">
       Resolution 819
      </a>
      , which demanded that: "all parties and others concerned treat Srebrenica and its surroundings as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safe_area_(Bosnian_War)" title="Safe area (Bosnian War)">
       safe area
      </a>
      which should be free from any armed attack or any other hostile act".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UN2-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 18 April 1993, the first group of UNPROFOR troops arrived in Srebrenica. On 8 May 1993 agreement was reached of demilitarization of Srebrenica. According to UN reports "General [Sefer] Halilovi and General [Ratko] Mladi agreed on measures covering the whole of the Srebrenica enclave and the adjacent enclave of epa. Under the terms of the new agreement, Bosniak forces within the enclave would hand over their weapons, ammunition and mines to UNPROFOR, after which Serb "heavy weapons and units that constituted a menace to the demilitarized zones which will have been established in epa and Srebrenica will be withdrawn." Unlike the earlier agreement, the agreement of 8 May stated specifically that Srebrenica was to be considered a "demilitarized zone", as referred to in article 60 of the Protocol Additional to the Geneva Conventions of 12 August 1949, and relating to the Protection of Victims of International Armed Conflicts (Protocol I)."
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1,000 and 2,000 soldiers from three of the VRS Drina Corps
      <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">
       Brigades
      </a>
      were deployed around the enclave, equipped with tanks, armoured vehicles, artillery and
      <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">
       mortars
      </a>
      . The 28th Mountain Division of the
      <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republic_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Army of the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       Army of the Republic of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      (ARBiH) remaining in the enclave was neither well organised nor equipped: a firm command structure and communications system was lacking and some soldiers carried old hunting rifles or no weapons at all. Few had proper uniforms.
     </p>
     <p>
      From the outset, both parties to the conflict violated the "safe area" agreement.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant-Colonel" title="Lieutenant-Colonel">
       Lieutenant-Colonel
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Karremans" title="Thomas Karremans">
       Thomas Karremans
      </a>
      (the
      <a href="/wiki/Dutchbat" title="Dutchbat">
       Dutchbat
      </a>
      Commander) testified to the ICTY that his personnel were prevented from returning to the enclave by Serb forces and that equipment and ammunition were also prevented from getting in.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bosniaks in Srebrenica complained of attacks by Serb soldiers, while to the Serbs it appeared that Bosnian government forces in Srebrenica were using the "safe area" as a convenient base from which to launch counter-offensives against the Army of the Republika Srpska (VRS) and that UNPROFOR was failing to take any action to prevent it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      General
      <a href="/wiki/Sefer_Halilovi%C4%87" title="Sefer Halilovi">
       Sefer Halilovi
      </a>
      admitted that ARBiH helicopters had flown in violation of the no-fly zone and that he had personally dispatched eight helicopters with ammunition for the 28th Division.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Serb_refusal_to_demilitarise_around_Srebrenica">
       Serb refusal to demilitarise around Srebrenica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Serb refusal to demilitarise around Srebrenica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A Security Council mission led by
      <a href="/wiki/Diego_Arria" title="Diego Arria">
       Diego Arria
      </a>
      arrived in Srebrenica on 25 April 1993 and, in their subsequent report to the U.N., condemned the Serbs for perpetrating "a slow-motion process of genocide."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report_on_The_Fall_of_Srebrenica_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Report_on_The_Fall_of_Srebrenica-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The mission then stated that "Serb forces must withdraw to points from which they cannot attack, harass or terrorise the town. UNPROFOR should be in a position to determine the related parameters. The mission believes, as does UNPROFOR, that the actual 4.5km by 0.5km decided as a safe area should be greatly expanded." Specific instructions from United Nations Headquarters in New York stated that UNPROFOR should not be too zealous in searching for Bosniak weapons and, later, that the Serbs should withdraw their heavy weapons before the Bosniaks gave up their weapons. The Serbs never did withdraw their heavy weapons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report_on_The_Fall_of_Srebrenica_52-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Report_on_The_Fall_of_Srebrenica-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_1995:_the_situation_in_the_Srebrenica_.22safe_area.22_deteriorates">
       Early 1995: the situation in the Srebrenica "safe area" deteriorates
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title='Edit section: Early 1995: the situation in the Srebrenica "safe area" deteriorates'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      By early 1995, fewer and fewer supply convoys were making it through to the enclave. The situation in Srebrenica and in other enclaves had deteriorated into lawless violence as prostitution among young Muslim girls, theft and black marketeering proliferated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The already meager resources of the civilian population dwindled further and even the UN forces started running dangerously low on food, medicine, ammunition and fuel, eventually being forced to start patrolling the enclave on foot. Dutchbat soldiers who went out of the area on leave were not allowed to return
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNGA_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UNGA-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and their number dropped from 600
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      to 400 men. In March and April, the Dutch soldiers noticed a build-up of Serb forces near two of the observation posts, "OP Romeo" and "OP Quebec".
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 1995,
      <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan Karadi">
       Radovan Karadi
      </a>
      , President of the Republika Srpska (RS), despite pressure from the international community to end the war and ongoing efforts to negotiate a peace agreement, issued a directive to the VRS concerning the long-term strategy of the VRS forces in the enclave. The directive, known as "Directive 7", specified that the VRS was to:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Complete the physical separation of Srebrenica from epa as soon as possible, preventing even communication between individuals in the two enclaves. By planned and well-thought out combat operations, create an unbearable situation of total insecurity with no hope of further survival or life for the inhabitants of Srebrenica.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY2_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICTY2-55">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         55
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      By mid-1995, the humanitarian situation of the Bosniak civilians and military personnel in the enclave was catastrophic. In May, following orders, Ori and his staff left the enclave by helicopter to
      <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">
       Tuzla
      </a>
      , leaving senior officers in command of the 28th Division. In late June and early July, the 28th Division issued a series of reports including urgent pleas for the
      <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_corridor" title="Humanitarian corridor">
       humanitarian corridor
      </a>
      to the enclave to be reopened. When this failed, Bosniak civilians began dying from starvation. On Friday, 7 July the mayor of Srebrenica reported 8 residents had died of starvation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="4_June_and_6.E2.80.9311_July_1995:_Serb_take-over_of_Srebrenica">
       4 June and 611 July 1995: Serb take-over of Srebrenica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 4 June and 611 July 1995: Serb take-over of Srebrenica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 4 June 1995, the the commander of the UN forces in former Yugoslavia, general
      <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Janvier" title="Bernard Janvier">
       Bernard Janvier
      </a>
      - from France - secretly met with Ratko Mladi to obtain the release of hostages, many of whom were French. Mladi demanded of Janvier that there would be no more air strikes.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Serb offensive against Srebrenica began in earnest on 6 July 1995. In the following days, the five UNPROFOR observation posts in the southern part of the enclave fell one by one in the face of the Bosnian Serb advance. Some of the Dutch soldiers retreated into the enclave after their posts were attacked, but the crews of the other observation posts surrendered into Serb
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_custody" title="Police custody">
       custody
      </a>
      . Simultaneously, the defending Bosnian forces came under heavy fire and were pushed back towards the town. Once the southern perimeter began to collapse, about 4,000 Bosniak residents who had been living in a Swedish housing complex for refugees nearby fled north into the town of Srebrenica. Dutch soldiers reported that the advancing Serbs were "cleansing" the houses in the southern part of the enclave.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1352" data-file-width="1799" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg/220px-Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg/330px-Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg/440px-Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pantserrupsvoertuig_YPR-765.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A Dutch YPR-765
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
         <a href="#cite_note-58">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          58
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 8 July, a Dutch
      <a href="/wiki/AIFV" title="AIFV">
       YPR-765
      </a>
      armoured vehicle took fire from the Serbs and withdrew. A group of Bosniaks demanded that the armoured vehicle stay to defend them. As the armoured vehicle continued to withdraw, a Bosniak man threw a hand grenade onto it and subsequently killed Dutch soldier Raviv van Renssen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Late on 9 July 1995, emboldened by early successes and little resistance from the largely demilitarised Bosniaks as well as the absence of any significant reaction from the international community, the President of the Republika Srpska, Radovan Karadi, issued a new order authorising the 1,500-strong
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      VRS Drina Corps to capture the town of Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On the morning of 10 July 1995, the situation in Srebrenica was tense. Residents crowded the streets. The Dutch UNPROFOR troops fired warning shots over the heads of the attacking Bosnian Serbs and their mortars fired flares but they never fired directly on any Serb units. Lieutenant-Colonel Karremans sent repeated urgent requests for
      <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
       NATO
      </a>
      air support to defend the town, but no assistance was forthcoming until around 2:30pm on 11 July 1995, when 2 Dutch F-16's guided by
      <a href="/wiki/Korps_Commandotroepen" title="Korps Commandotroepen">
       Dutch KCT
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Special_Air_Service" title="Special Air Service">
       British SAS
      </a>
      bombed VRS tanks advancing towards the town. NATO planes also attempted to bomb VRS artillery positions overlooking the town, but had to abort the operation because of poor visibility. NATO plans to continue the air strikes were abandoned following the VRS's threats to kill Dutch troops and the French hostages (pilots in the custody of the VRS), as well as to shell the UN Potoari compound on the outside of the town, and surrounding areas where 20,000 to 30,000 civilians had fled.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Late in the afternoon of 11 July, General Mladi, accompanied by General ivanovi (then-Commander of the Drina Corps), General Krsti (then-Deputy Commander and Chief of Staff of the Drina Corps) and other VRS officers, took a triumphant walk through the deserted streets of the town of Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the evening,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Lieutenant-Colonel
      <a href="/wiki/Thom_Karremans" title="Thom Karremans">
       Thom Karremans
      </a>
      was filmed drinking a toast with General Mladi during the bungled negotiations on the fate of the civilian population grouped in Potoari.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daruvalla_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Daruvalla-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Massacre">
       Massacre
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Massacre">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The two highest ranking Serb politicians from Bosnia and Herzegovina, Karadi and
      <a href="/wiki/Mom%C4%8Dilo_Kraji%C5%A1nik" title="Momilo Krajinik">
       Momilo Krajinik
      </a>
      , both indicted for genocide, were warned by military commander General Mladi (also indicted on genocide charges) that their plans could not be realised without committing genocide. Mladi said:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       People are not little stones, or keys in someone's pocket, that can be moved from one place to another just like that.... Therefore, we cannot precisely arrange for only Serbs to stay in one part of the country while removing others painlessly. I do not know how Mr. Krajinik and Mr. Karadi will explain that to the world. That is genocide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         64
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="11.E2.80.9313_July_1995:_the_increasing_concentration_of_refugees_in_Poto.C4.8Dari">
       1113 July 1995: the increasing concentration of refugees in Potoari
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1113 July 1995: the increasing concentration of refugees in Potoari">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg/220px-Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg/330px-Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg/440px-Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dutchbat_HQ_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Headquarters in
        <a href="/wiki/Donji_Poto%C4%8Dari" title="Donji Potoari">
         Potoari
        </a>
        for soldiers under
        <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
         United Nations
        </a>
        command; "
        <a href="/wiki/Dutchbat" title="Dutchbat">
         Dutchbat
        </a>
        " had 370
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
         <a href="#cite_note-65">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          65
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        soldiers in Srebrenica during the massacre. The building was a disused battery factory
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      By the evening of 11 July 1995, approximately 20,000 to 25,000 Bosniak refugees from Srebrenica were gathered in Potoari, seeking protection within the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNPROFOR" title="UNPROFOR">
       UNPROFOR
      </a>
      Dutchbat headquarters. Several thousand had pressed inside the compound itself, while the rest were spread throughout the neighbouring factories and fields. Though the vast majority were women, children, elderly or disabled, 63 witnesses estimated that there were at least 300 men inside the perimeter of the UNPROFOR compound and between 600 and 900 men in the crowd outside.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      UNPROFOR Dutchbat soldiers [on site] claimed
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      their base was full.
     </p>
     <p>
      Conditions in Potoari included "little food or water available" and sweltering heat. One UNPROFOR Dutchbat officer described the scene as follows:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       They were panicked, they were scared, and they were pressing each other against the soldiers, my soldiers, the UN soldiers that tried to calm them. People that fell were trampled on. It was a chaotic situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         51
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      On 12 July, the United Nations Security Council, in
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1004" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1004">
       Resolution 1004
      </a>
      , expressed concern at the humanitarian situation in Potoari, which also condemned the offensive by Bosnian Serb forces and demanded immediate withdrawal.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 July, the Dutch forces expelled
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="(July 2015)">
          why?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      five Bosniak refugees from the United Nations compound although knowing that men outside the compound were being killed and abused.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9613_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT9613-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="12.E2.80.9313_July:_crimes_committed_in_Poto.C4.8Dari">
       1213 July: crimes committed in Potoari
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1213 July: crimes committed in Potoari">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 12 July 1995, as the day wore on, the refugees in the compound could see VRS soldiers setting houses and haystacks on fire. Throughout the afternoon, Serb soldiers mingled in the crowd and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summary_executions" title="Summary executions">
       summary executions
      </a>
      of men occurred.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the late morning of 12 July 1995 a witness saw a pile of 20 to 30 bodies heaped up behind the Transport Building in Potoari, alongside a tractor-like machine. Another testified that he saw a soldier slay a child with a knife in the middle of a crowd of expellees. He also said that he saw Serb soldiers execute more than a hundred Bosnian Muslim men in the area behind the Zinc Factory and then load their bodies onto a truck, although the number and nature of the murders stand in contrast to other evidence on the Trial Record which indicates that the killings in Potoari were sporadic in nature. Soldiers were picking people out of the crowd and taking them away. A witness recounted how three brothers  one merely a child and the others in their teens  were taken out in the night. When the boys' mother went looking for them, she found them stark naked and with their throats slit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      That night, a Dutchbat medical orderly witnessed two Serb soldiers raping a young woman.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One survivor described the murder of a baby and the rape of women occurring in the close vicinity of Dutch U.N. peacekeepers who did nothing to prevent it. According to the survivor, a Serb told a mother to make her child stop crying, and when it continued to cry he took it and slit its throat, after which he laughed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stories about rapes and killings spread through the crowd and the terror in the camp escalated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Several individuals were so terrified that they committed suicide by hanging themselves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One of the survivors, Zarfa Turkovic,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      described the horrors of rapes as follows: "Two [Serb soldiers] took her legs and raised them up in the air, while the third began raping her. Four of them were taking turns on her. People were silent, no one moved. She was screaming and yelling and begging them to stop. They put a rag into her mouth and then we just heard silent sobs...."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Separation_and_murder_of_Bosniak_men_and_boys_in_Poto.C4.8Dari">
       Separation and murder of Bosniak men and boys in Potoari
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Separation and murder of Bosniak men and boys in Potoari">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      From the morning of 12 July, Serb forces began gathering men and boys from the refugee population in Potoari and holding them in separate locations, and as the refugees began boarding the buses headed north towards Bosniak-held territory, Serb soldiers separated out men of military age who were trying to clamber aboard. Occasionally, younger and older men were stopped as well (some as young as 14 or 15).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These men were taken to a building in Potoari referred to as the "White House". As early as the evening of 12 July 1995, Major Franken of the Dutchbat heard that no men were arriving with the women and children at their destination in
      <a href="/wiki/Kladanj" title="Kladanj">
       Kladanj
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At this time, the UNHCR Director of Operations, Peter Walsh, was dispatched to Srebrenica by the UNHCR Chief of Mission, Damaso Feci, to evaluate what emergency aid could be provided rapidly. Peter Walsh and his team arrived at Gostilj, just outside Srebrenica, in the early afternoon only to be turned away by VRS forces. Despite claiming freedom of movement rights, the UNHCR team was not allowed to proceed and was forced to head back north to Bijelina. Throughout this time, Peter Walsh relayed reports back to UNHCR in Zagreb about the unfolding situation including witnessing the enforced movement and abuse of Muslim men and boys and the sound of summary executions taking place.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 July 1995, Dutchbat troops witnessed definite signs that the Serb soldiers were murdering some of the Bosniak men who had been separated. For example, Corporal Vaasen saw two soldiers take a man behind the "White House", heard a shot and saw the two soldiers reappear alone. Another Dutchbat officer saw Serb soldiers murder an unarmed man with a single gunshot to the head and heard gunshots 2040 times an hour throughout the afternoon. When the Dutchbat soldiers told Colonel Joseph Kingori, a
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Military_Observer" title="United Nations Military Observer">
       United Nations Military Observer
      </a>
      (UNMO) in the Srebrenica area, that men were being taken behind the "White House" and not coming back, Colonel Kingori went to investigate. He heard gunshots as he approached, but was stopped by Serb soldiers before he could find out what was going on.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some of the executions were carried out at night under arc lights, and industrial bulldozers then pushed the bodies into mass graves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-2006-05-03_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-2006-05-03-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to evidence collected from Bosniaks by French policeman Jean-Ren Ruez, some were buried alive; he also heard testimony describing Serb forces killing and torturing refugees at will, streets littered with corpses, people committing suicide to avoid having their noses, lips and ears chopped off, and adults being forced to watch the soldiers kill their children.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN-2006-05-03_74-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-2006-05-03-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Rape_and_abuse_of_civilians">
       Rape and abuse of civilians
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rape and abuse of civilians">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Many women and girls suffered rape and sexual abuse and other forms of torture. According to the testimony of Zumra ehomerovic:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       The Serbs began at a certain point to take girls and young women out of the group of refugees. They were raped. The rapes often took place under the eyes of others and sometimes even under the eyes of the children of the mother. A Dutch soldier stood by and he simply looked around with a
       <a href="/wiki/Walkman" title="Walkman">
        Walkman
       </a>
       on his head. He did not react at all to what was happening. It did not happen just before my eyes, for I saw that personally, but also before the eyes of us all. The Dutch soldiers walked around everywhere. It is impossible that they did not see it.
      </p>
      <p>
       There was a woman with a small baby a few months old. A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chetnik" title="Chetnik">
        Chetnik
       </a>
       told the mother that the child must stop crying. When the child did not stop crying, he snatched the child away and cut its throat. Then he laughed. There was a Dutch soldier there who was watching. He did not react at all.
      </p>
      <p>
       I saw yet more frightful things. For example, there was a girl, she must have been about nine years old. At a certain moment some Chetniks recommended to her brother that he rape the girl. He did not do it and I also think that he could not have done it for he was still just a child. Then they murdered that young boy. I have personally seen all that. I really want to emphasize that all this happened in the immediate vicinity of the base. In the same way I also saw other people who were murdered. Some of them had their throats cut. Others were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Behead" title="Behead">
        beheaded
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         75
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Testimony of Ramiza Gurdi:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       I saw how a young boy of about ten was killed by Serbs in Dutch uniform. This happened in front of my own eyes. The mother sat on the ground and her young son sat beside her. The young boy was placed on his mother's lap. The young boy was killed. His head was cut off. The body remained on the lap of the mother. The Serbian soldier placed the head of the young boy on his knife and showed it to everyone.  I saw how a pregnant woman was slaughtered. There were Serbs who stabbed her in the stomach, cut her open and took two small children out of her stomach and then beat them to death on the ground. I saw this with my own eyes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         76
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Testimony of Kada Hoti:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       There was a young woman with a baby on the way to the bus. The baby cried and a Serbian soldier told her that she had to make sure that the baby was quiet. Then the soldier took the child from the mother and cut its throat. I do not know whether Dutchbat soldiers saw that.  There was a sort of fence on the left-hand side of the road to Potocari. I heard then a young woman screaming very close by (4 or 5 meters away). I then heard another woman beg: "Leave her, she is only nine years old." The screaming suddenly stopped. I was so in shock that I could scarcely move.  The rumour later quickly circulated that a nine year old girl had been raped.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         77
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      That night, a Dutch Bat medical orderly came across two Serb soldiers raping a young woman:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       "[W]e saw two Serb soldiers, one of them was standing guard and the other one was lying on the girl, with his pants off. And we saw a girl lying on the ground, on some kind of mattress. There was blood on the mattress, even she was covered with blood. She had bruises on her legs. There was even blood coming down her legs. She was in total shock. She went totally crazy."
      </p>
      <p>
       Bosnian Muslim refugees nearby could see the rape, but could do nothing about it because of Serb soldiers standing nearby. Other people heard women screaming, or saw women being dragged away. Several individuals were so terrified that they committed suicide by hanging themselves. Throughout the night and early the next morning, stories about the rapes and killings spread through the crowd and the terror in the camp escalated.
      </p>
      <p>
       Screams, gunshots and other frightening noises were audible throughout the night and no one could sleep. Soldiers were picking people out of the crowd and taking them away: some returned; others did not. Witness T recounted how three brothers  one merely a child and the others in their teens  were taken out in the night. When the boys' mother went looking for them, she found them with their throats slit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         78
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Deportation_of_women">
       Deportation of women
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Deportation of women">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      As a result of exhaustive UN negotiations with Serb troops, around 25,000 Srebrenica women were forcibly transferred to the Bosniak-controlled territory.
     </p>
     <p>
      Some buses apparently never reached safety. According to a witness account given by Kadir Habibovi, who hid himself on one of the first buses from the base in Potoari to Kladanj, he saw at least one vehicle full of Bosniak women being driven away from Bosnian government-held territory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhode_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Rhode-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
