      <span class="mw-headline" id="Column_of_Bosniak_men">
       Column of Bosniak men
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Column of Bosniak men">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On the evening of 11 July 1995, word spread through the Bosniak community that able-bodied men should take to the woods, form a column together with members of the ARBiH's 28th Division and attempt a breakthrough towards Bosnian government-held territory in the north.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The men believed they stood a better chance of surviving by trying to escape than if they let themselves fall into Serb hands.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="697" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_massacre_map.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Map of military operations during the Srebrenica massacre. Green arrow marks route of the Bosnian column
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Around 10pm on 11 July the Division command, together with the municipal authorities, took the decision, on their own initiative, to form a column and leave the safe area in an attempt to reach government-controlled territory around Tuzla.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty.org_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty.org-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The journey to Tuzla  a distance of 55 kilometres  entailed crossing extremely hilly terrain in the height of the summer heat. Most individuals started out with enough rations for only two days; by the third day, people were beginning to eat leaves and slugs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailymail.co.uk_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-dailymail.co.uk-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Dehydration made finding drinking water a major problem, along with lack of sleep and physical exhaustion  many were exhausted before setting out. There was little cohesion or sense of common purpose in the column.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Along the way, the column was shelled and ambushed. In severe mental distress, some of the refugees committed suicide. Others were induced to surrender. Survivors claimed they were attacked with a chemical agent that caused hallucinations, disorientation and strange behaviour.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popovic_2006_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Popovic_2006-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commdocs.house.gov_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-commdocs.house.gov-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sense-agency.com_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sense-agency.com-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Infiltrators in civilian clothing confused, attacked and killed refugees, including the wounded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many of those taken prisoner were killed on the spot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Others were collected together before being taken to remote locations for mass execution.
     </p>
     <p>
      The attacks on the column broke it up into smaller segments. Only about one third of the men succeeded in crossing the asphalt road between Konjevi Polje and Nova Kasaba. It was this group that eventually crossed Bosnian Serb lines to reach Bosnian government territory on and after 16 July. The vast majority of the victims of the massacre were members of the column who failed to complete the perilous journey.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_groups">
       Other groups
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other groups">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A second, smaller group of refugees (estimated at between 700 and 800) attempted to escape into Serbia via Mount Kvarac via Bratunac, or across the River Drina and via
      <a href="/wiki/Bajina_Ba%C5%A1ta" title="Bajina Bata">
       Bajina Bata
      </a>
      . It is not known how many were intercepted, arrested and killed on the way. A third group headed for epa, possibly having first tried to reach Tuzla. The estimates of the numbers involved vary widely, from 300 to around 850. In addition, small pockets of resistance apparently remained behind and engaged Serb forces.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tuzla_column_departs">
       Tuzla column departs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Tuzla column departs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Almost all the 28th Division, 5500 to 6000 soldiers, not all armed, gathered in the village of Susnjari, in the hills north of the town of Srebrenica, along with about 7,000 civilians. They included a very small number of women, not more than ten.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Others assembled in the nearby village of Jaglici.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At around midnight on 11 July 1995, the column started moving along the axis between Konjevi Polje and Bratunac. The main column was preceded by a reconnaissance party of four scouts, approximately five kilometres ahead.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Members of the column walked one behind the other, following the paper trail laid down by a de-mining unit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1083_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1083-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The column was led by a group of 50100 of the best soldiers from each brigade, carrying the best available equipment. Elements of the 284th Brigade were followed by the 280th Brigade, with them the Chief of Staff Ramiz Becirovic. Civilians accompanied by other soldiers followed and at the back was the independent battalion which was part of the 28th Division.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty.org_82-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty.org-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The elite of the enclave, including the mother and sister of Naser Ori
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      , accompanied the best troops at the front of the column.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1083_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1083-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Others in the column included the political leaders of the enclave, medical staff of the local hospital and the families of prominent persons in Srebrenica. A small number of women, children and elderly travelled with the column in the woods.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_80-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neth-WarDocs_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Neth-WarDocs-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Each brigade was responsible for a group of refugees and many civilians joined the military units spontaneously as the journey got underway
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The column was between 12 and 15 kilometres long, about two and a half hours separating head from tail.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty.org_82-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty.org-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The breakout from the enclave and the attempt to reach Tuzla came as a surprise to the VRS and caused considerable confusion, as the VRS had expected the men to go to Potoari. Serb general
      <a href="/wiki/Milan_Gvero" title="Milan Gvero">
       Milan Gvero
      </a>
      in a briefing referred to members of the column as "
      <i>
       hardened and violent criminals who will stop at nothing to prevent being taken prisoner and to enable their escape into Bosnian territory.
      </i>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Drina Corps and the various brigades were ordered by the VRS Main Staff to assign all available manpower to the task of finding any Muslim groups observed, preventing them from crossing into Muslim territory, taking them prisoner and holding them in buildings that could be secured by small forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ambush_at_Kamenica_Hill">
       Ambush at Kamenica Hill
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ambush at Kamenica Hill">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      During the night, poor visibility, fear of mines and panic induced by artillery fire split the column in two.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch.org_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch.org-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On the afternoon of 12 July, the front section emerged from the woods and crossed the asphalt road from Konjevic Polje and Nova Kasaba. Around 18.00 hours, the RS Army located the main part of the column still in the hilly area around Kamenica (outside the village of
      <a href="/wiki/Pobu%C4%91e" title="Pobue">
       Pobue
      </a>
      ). Around 20.00 hours this part of the column, led by the municipal authorities and the wounded, started descending Kamenica Hill (
      <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
       <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;params=44_19_53_N_18_14_5_E_type:mountain&amp;title=Karmenica">
        <span class="geo-default">
         <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
          <span class="latitude">
           441953N
          </span>
          <span class="longitude">
           18145E
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          / 
        </span>
        <span class="geo-nondefault">
         <span class="vcard">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           44.33139N 18.23472E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            /
           <span class="geo">
            44.33139; 18.23472
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            (
           <span class="fn org">
            Karmenica
           </span>
           )
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
      </span>
      ) towards the road. After a few dozen men had crossed, soldiers of the RS Army arrived from the direction of Kravica in trucks and armored vehicles including a white vehicle with UNPROFOR symbols, calling out for Bosniaks over the loudspeaker to surrender.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch.org_98-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch.org-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was around this time that yellow smoke was observed, followed by observations of strange behaviour, including suicides, hallucinations and members of the column attacking one another.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Popovic_2006_85-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Popovic_2006-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Numerous survivors interviewed by Human Rights Watch claimed they were attacked with a chemical agent that caused hallucinations and disorientation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commdocs.house.gov_86-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-commdocs.house.gov-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_87-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (Gen. Zdravko Tolimir was an advocate of the use of chemical weapons against the ArBiH.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sense-agency.com_88-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sense-agency.com-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      )
     </p>
     <p>
      Heavy shooting and shelling began, which continued into the night. The armed members of the column returned fire and all scattered. Survivors describe a group of at least 1000 engaged at close range by small arms. Hundreds appear to have been killed as they fled the open area and some were said to have killed themselves to escape capture.
     </p>
     <p>
      RS Army and Ministry of Interior persuaded members of the column to surrender by promising them protection and safe transportation towards Tuzla under UNPROFOR and Red Cross supervision. Appropriated UN and Red Cross equipment was used to deceive the refugees into believing the promises. Surrendering prisoners' personal belongings were confiscated and some were executed on the spot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch.org_98-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch.org-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The rear of the column lost contact with the front and panic broke out. Many people remained in the Kamenica Hill area for a number of days, unable to move on with the escape route blocked by Serb forces. Thousands of Bosniaks surrendered or were captured. Some prisoners were ordered to summon friends and family members from the woods. There were reports of Serb forces using megaphones to call on the marchers to surrender, telling them that they would be exchanged for Serb soldiers held captive by Bosniak forces. It was at Kamenica that VRS personnel in civilian dress were reported to have infiltrated the column.
     </p>
     <p>
      Men from the rear of the column who survived this ordeal described it as a manhunt.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_80-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radislav_Krsti.C4.87_verdict_.E2.80.93_The_Column_of_Bosnian_Muslim_Men-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sandi.C4.87i_massacre">
       Sandii massacre
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sandii massacre">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="286" data-file-width="432" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg/220px-Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg/330px-Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Exhumations_in_Srebrenica_1996.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhumation" title="Exhumation">
         Exhumations
        </a>
        in Srebrenica, 1996
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Close to Sandii, on the main road from Bratunac to Konjevi Polje, one witness describes the Serbs forcing a Bosniak man to call other Bosniaks down from the mountains. Some 200 to 300 men, including the witness' brother, followed his instructions and descended to meet the VRS, presumably expecting some exchange of prisoners would take place. The witness hid behind a tree to see what would happen next. He watched as the men were lined up in seven ranks, each some forty metres in length, with their hands behind their heads; they were then mowed down by machine gun fire.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3665_100-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3665-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The VRS also sent one of the civilians who wished to surrender back towards the column: one of his eyes had been gouged out, his ears had been cut off and a cross carved into his forehead.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A small number of women, children and elderly people who had been part of the column were allowed to join the buses evacuating the women and children out of Potoari. Among them was Alma Delimustafi, a soldier of the 28th Brigade; at this time, Delimustafi was in her civilian clothes and was released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Trek_to_Mount_Udrc">
       Trek to Mount Udrc
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Trek to Mount Udrc">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The central section of the column managed to escape the shooting and reached Kamenica at about 11.00 hours and waited there for the wounded.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_(land)" title="Captain (land)">
       Captain
      </a>
      Ejub Goli and the Independent Battalion turned back towards Hajduko Groblje to help the casualties. A number of survivors from the rear, who managed to escape crossed the asphalt roads to the north or the west of the area, had joined those in the central section of the column. The front third of the column, which had already left Kamenica Hill by the time the ambush occurred, headed for Mount Udrc (
      <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
       <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;params=44_16_59_N_19_3_6_E_type:mountain&amp;title=Mount+Udrc">
        <span class="geo-default">
         <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
          <span class="latitude">
           441659N
          </span>
          <span class="longitude">
           1936E
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          / 
        </span>
        <span class="geo-nondefault">
         <span class="vcard">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           44.28306N 19.05167E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            /
           <span class="geo">
            44.28306; 19.05167
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            (
           <span class="fn org">
            Mount Udrc
           </span>
           )
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
      </span>
      ); crossing the main asphalt road, they then forded the river Jadar. They reached the base of the mountain early on the morning of Thursday, 13 July and regrouped. At first, it was decided to send 300 ARBiH soldiers back in an attempt to break through the blockades. When reports came in that the central section of the column had nevertheless succeeded in crossing the road at Konjevi Polje, this plan was abandoned. Approximately 1,000 additional men managed to reach Udrc that night.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Snagovo_ambush">
       Snagovo ambush
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Snagovo ambush">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      From Udrc the marchers moved toward the River Drinjaka and on to Mount Velja Glava, continuing through the night. Finding a Serb presence at Mount Velja Glava, where they arrived on Friday, 14 July the column was forced to skirt the mountain and wait on its slopes before it was able to move on toward Liplje and Marcici. Arriving at Marcici in the evening of 14 July the marchers were again ambushed near Snagovo by Serb forces equipped with anti-aircraft guns, artillery, and tanks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      According to Lieutenant Demail Beirovi, the column managed to break through the ambush and, in so doing, captured a VRS officer, Major Zoran Jankoviproviding the Army of Bosnia and Herzegovina with a significant bargaining counter. This prompted an attempt at negotiating a cessation in the fighting, but negotiations with local Serb forces failed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, the act of repulsing the ambush had a positive effect on morale of the marchers, who also captured an amount of weapons and supplies.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Approaching_the_frontline">
       Approaching the frontline
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Approaching the frontline">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The evening of 15 July saw the first radio contact between the 2nd Corps and the 28th Division, established using a
      <a href="/wiki/Walkie-talkie" title="Walkie-talkie">
       walkie-talkie
      </a>
      captured from the VRS. After initial distrust on the part of the 28th Division, the brothers abi were able to identify each other as they stood on either side of the VRS lines. Early in the morning, the column crossed the asphalt road linking Zvornik with Caparde and headed in the direction of Planinci, leaving a unit of some 100 to 200 armed marchers behind to wait for stragglers.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The column reached Krizevici later that day, and remained there while an attempt was made to negotiate with local Serb forces for safe passage through the Serb lines into Bosnian government controlled territory. The members of the column were advised to stay where they were, and to allow the Serb forces time to arrange for safe passage. It soon became apparent, though, that the small Serb force deployed in the area was only trying to gain time to organise a further attack on the marchers. In the area of Marcici-Crni the RS armed forces deployed 500 soldiers and policemen in order to stop the split part of the column (about 2,500 people), which was moving from Glodi towards Marcici.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At this point, the column's leaders decided to form several small groups of between 100 and 200 persons and send these to reconnoiter the way ahead. Early in the afternoon, the 2nd Corps and the 28th Division of the ARBiH met each other in the village of Potocani. The presidium of Srebrenica were the first to reach Bosnian terrain.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Breakthrough_at_Baljkovica">
       Breakthrough at Baljkovica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Breakthrough at Baljkovica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The hillside at Baljkovica (
      <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
       <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;params=44_27_N_18_58_E_type:city&amp;title=Baljkovica">
        <span class="geo-default">
         <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
          <span class="latitude">
           4427N
          </span>
          <span class="longitude">
           1858E
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          / 
        </span>
        <span class="geo-nondefault">
         <span class="vcard">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           44.450N 18.967E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            /
           <span class="geo">
            44.450; 18.967
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            (
           <span class="fn org">
            Baljkovica
           </span>
           )
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
      </span>
      ) formed the last VRS line separating the column from Bosnian-held territory. The VRS cordon actually consisted of two lines, the first of which presented a front on the Tuzla side against the 2nd Corps and the other a front against the approaching 28th Division.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On the evening of 15 July a heavy hailstorm caused the Serb forces to take cover. The column's advance group took advantage of this to attack the Serb rear lines at Baljkovica. During the fighting, the main body of what remained of the column began to move from Krizevici. It reached the area of fighting at about 3am on Sunday, 16 July.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At approximately 05.00 hours on 16 July, the 2nd Corps made its first attempt to break through the VRS cordon from the Bosnian side. The objective was to force a breakthrough close to the hamlets of Parlog and Resnik. They were joined by Naser Ori and a number of his men.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Around 8am on the morning of 16 July parts of the 28th Division, with the 2nd Corps of the RBiH Army from Tuzla providing artillery support, attacked and breached RS Army lines. There was fierce fighting across the general area of Baljkovica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Captured heavy arms including two Praga
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-propelled_anti-aircraft" title="Self-propelled anti-aircraft">
       self-propelled anti-aircraft
      </a>
      guns were fired at the Serb front line and the column finally succeeded in breaking through to Bosnian government controlled territory and linking up with BiH units at between 1pm and 2pm on 16 July.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Baljkovica_corridor">
       Baljkovica corridor
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Baljkovica corridor">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Following radio negotiations between the 2nd Corps and the Zvornik Brigade, the Zvornik Brigade Command, which had lost three lines of trenches, agreed to open a corridor to allow "evacuation" of the column in return for the release of captured policemen and soldiers. The Baljkovica corridor was open from 14.00 to 17.00 hours.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After the corridor was closed between 17.00 and 18.00 hours the Zvornik Brigade Command reported that around 5000 civilians, with probably "a certain number of soldiers" with them had been let through, but "all those who passed were unarmed".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_at_Tuzla">
       Arrival at Tuzla
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Arrival at Tuzla">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="2304" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_2008_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Damaged building in Srebrenica after the war
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Only a few journalists witnessed the arrival of the column in Bosnian-held territory, most attention was focused on the reception of the women and children at the airbase in Tuzla (
      <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">
       <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;params=44_27_31_N_18_43_31_E_type:landmark&amp;title=Tuzla">
        <span class="geo-default">
         <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
          <span class="latitude">
           442731N
          </span>
          <span class="longitude">
           184331E
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span class="geo-multi-punct">
          / 
        </span>
        <span class="geo-nondefault">
         <span class="vcard">
          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">
           44.45861N 18.72528E
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            /
           <span class="geo">
            44.45861; 18.72528
           </span>
          </span>
          <span style="display:none">
            (
           <span class="fn org">
            Tuzla
           </span>
           )
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </a>
      </span>
      ). The few press and television reports described the arrival of 'an army of ghosts': men clad in rags, totally exhausted and emaciated by hunger. Some had no more than underwear, some were walking on bleeding feet wrapped in rags or plastic, and some were being carried on makeshift stretchers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailymail.co.uk_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-dailymail.co.uk-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There were men walking hand in hand with children; many were still visibly frightened. Some were
      <a href="/wiki/Delirium" title="Delirium">
       delirious
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hallucination" title="Hallucination">
       hallucinating
      </a>
      as a result of the immense stress they had endured. One soldier had begun firing on men in his own unit as they arrived in Baljkovica and was killed to prevent further bloodshed; the medical station set up by the Army of Bosnia and Herzegovina in
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Me%C4%91e%C4%91a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Meea (page does not exist)">
       Meea
      </a>
      handed out large quantities of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tranquilliser" title="Tranquilliser">
       tranquillisers
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The survivors felt bitterness towards the UN because it had not been able to protect the "Safe Area." Bitterness and resentment was also directed towards the 2nd Corps of the ARBiH and there were a number of incidents. In one, a member of the 28th Division opened fire at the Corps Commander,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sead_Deli%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sead Deli (page does not exist)">
       Sead Deli
      </a>
      , who had resisted all calls from his officers for a military push to link up with fleeing soldiers and civilians; a
      <a href="/wiki/Military_police" title="Military police">
       military police
      </a>
      bodyguard was killed, while another returned fire and killed the sniper. Tensions were so great that 2nd Corps staff officers removed their insignia in order to avoid recognition. According to the Deputy Corps Commander, the division had "turned against the 2nd Corps." This lack of confidence in the 2nd Corps was nothing new, however, as the 28th Division had felt abandoned already in Srebrenica.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By 4 August or thereabouts, the ArBiH determined that 3,175 members of the 28th Division had managed to get through to Tuzla. 2628 members of the Division, soldiers and officers, were considered certain to have been killed. The approximate number of individual members of the column killed was estimated at between 8300 and 9722.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_closure_of_the_corridor">
       After the closure of the corridor
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: After the closure of the corridor">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Once the corridor had closed Serb forces recommenced hunting down parts of the column still in areas under their control. Around 2,000 refugees were reported to be hiding in the woods in the area of Pobudje.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_108-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 17 July 1995, "searching the terrain", the RS Army captured a number of Bosniaks. Four children aged between 8 and 14 captured by the Bratunac Brigade were taken to the military barracks in Bratunac.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_108-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2005_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2005-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When one of them described seeing a large number of ARBiH soldiers committing suicide and shooting at each other,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Brigade Commander Blagojevi suggested that the Drina Corps' press unit should record this testimony on video.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2005_110-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2005-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The fate of the boys remains uncertain.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 18 July, after a soldier was killed "trying to capture some persons during the search operation", the Zvornik Brigade Command issued an order to execute prisoners in its zone of responsibility in order to avoid any risks associated with their capture. The order was presumed to have remained effective until it was countermanded on 21 July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_108-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plan_to_execute_the_men_of_Srebrenica">
       Plan to execute the men of Srebrenica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Plan to execute the men of Srebrenica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Although Serb forces had long been blamed for the massacre, it was not until June 2004following the Srebrenica commission's preliminary reportthat Serb officials acknowledged that their security forces planned and carried out the mass killing. A Serb commission's final report on the 1995 Srebrenica massacre acknowledged that the
      <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">
       mass murder
      </a>
      of the men and boys was planned. The commission found that more than 7,800 were killed after it compiled thirty-four
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      lists of victims.
     </p>
     <p>
      A concerted effort was made to capture all Bosniak men of military age.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In fact, those captured included many boys well below that age and elderly men several years above that age who remained in the enclave following the take-over of Srebrenica. These men and boys were targeted regardless of whether they chose to flee to Potoari or to join the Bosnian Muslim column. The operation to capture and detain the Bosnian Muslim men was well organised and comprehensive. The buses which transported the women and children were systematically searched for men.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_executions">
       Mass executions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mass executions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Mass_executions_in_the_Srebrenica_massacre" title="Mass executions in the Srebrenica massacre">
       Mass executions in the Srebrenica massacre
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The vast amount of planning and high-level coordination invested in killing thousands of men in a few days is apparent from the scale and the methodical nature in which the executions were carried out. A concerted effort was made to capture all Bosniak men of military age. In fact, those captured included many boys well below that age and elderly men above it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska" title="Army of Republika Srpska">
       Army of Republika Srpska
      </a>
      took the largest number of prisoners on 13 July, along the Bratunac-Konjevi Polje road. It remains impossible to cite a precise figure, but witness statements describe the assembly points such as the field at Sandii, the agricultural
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warehouses" title="Warehouses">
       warehouses
      </a>
      in Kravica, the school in Konjevi Polje, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_pitch" title="Association football pitch">
       football field
      </a>
      in Nova Kasaba, the village of Lolii and the village school of Luke. Several thousands of people were herded together in the field near Sandii and on the Nova Kasaba football pitch, where they were searched and put into smaller groups. In a video tape made by journalist Zoran Petrovi, a Serb soldier states that at least 3,000 to 4,000 men had given themselves up on the road. By the late afternoon of 13 July, the total had risen to some 6,000 according to the intercepted radio communication; the following day, Major Franken of Dutchbat was given the same figure by Colonel Radislav Jankovi of the Serb army. Many of the prisoners had been seen in the locations described by passing convoys taking the women and children to Kladanj by bus, while various aerial photographs have since provided evidence to confirm this version of events.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Neth-WarDocs_95-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Neth-WarDocs-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica_111-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One hour after the evacuation of the females from Potoari was completed, the Drina Corps staff diverted the buses to the areas in which the men were being held. Colonel Krsmanovi, who on 12 July had arranged the buses for the evacuation, ordered the 700 men in Sandii to be collected, and the soldiers guarding them made them throw their possessions on a large heap and hand over anything of value. During the afternoon, the group in Sandii was visited by Mladi who told them that they would come to no harm, that they would be treated as prisoners of war, that they would be exchanged for other prisoners and that their families had been escorted to Tuzla in safety. Some of these men were placed on the transport to Bratunac and other locations, while some were marched on foot to the warehouses in Kravica. The men gathered on the soccer ground at Nova Kasaba were forced to hand over their personal belongings. They too received a personal visit from Mladi during the afternoon of 13 July; on this occasion, he announced that the Bosnian authorities in Tuzla did not want the men and that they were therefore to be taken to other locations. The men in Nova Kasaba were loaded onto buses and trucks and were taken to Bratunac or the other locations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica_111-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Bosnian men who had been separated from the women, children and elderly in Potoari numbering approximately 1,000 were transported to Bratunac and subsequently joined by Bosnian men captured from the column.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Almost to a man
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2015)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      , the thousands of Bosnian prisoners captured, following the take-over of Srebrenica, were executed. Some were killed individually or in small groups by the soldiers who captured them and some were killed in the places where they were temporarily detained. Most, however, were killed in carefully orchestrated mass executions, commencing on 13 July 1995 in the region just north of Srebrenica.
     </p>
     <p>
      The mass executions followed a well-established pattern. The men were first taken to empty schools or warehouses. After being detained there for some hours, they were loaded onto buses or trucks and taken to another site for execution. Usually, the execution fields were in isolated locations. The prisoners were unarmed and in many cases, steps had been taken to minimise resistance, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Blindfold" title="Blindfold">
       blindfolding
      </a>
      them, binding their wrists behind their backs with ligatures or removing their shoes. Once at the killing fields, the men were taken off the trucks in small groups, lined up and shot. Those who survived the initial round of shooting were individually shot with an extra round, though sometimes only after they had been left to suffer for a time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica_111-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY:_Radoslav_Krsti.C4.87_.E2.80.93_A_Plan_to_Execute_the_Bosnian_Muslim_Men_of_Srebrenica-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The process of finding victim bodies in the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vlasenica_Region&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vlasenica Region (page does not exist)">
       Srebrenica region
      </a>
      , often in mass graves,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhumation" title="Exhumation">
       exhuming
      </a>
      them and finally identifying them was relatively slow.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Morning_of_13_July:_Jadar_River">
       Morning of 13 July: Jadar River
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Morning of 13 July: Jadar River">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A small-scale execution took place prior to midday at the Jadar River on 13 July. Seventeen men were transported by bus a short distance to a spot on the banks of the Jadar River. The men were then lined up and shot. One man, after being hit in the hip by a bullet, jumped into the river and managed to escape.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Afternoon_of_13_July:_Cerska_Valley">
       Afternoon of 13 July: Cerska Valley
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Afternoon of 13 July: Cerska Valley">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Massacre_Victim_2_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Skull of a victim of the July 1995 Srebrenica massacre. Exhumed mass grave outside the village of
        <a href="/wiki/Donji_Poto%C4%8Dari" title="Donji Potoari">
         Potocari
        </a>
        , Bosnia and Herzegovina. July 2007.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The first large-scale mass executions began on the afternoon of 13 July 1995 in the valley of the River Cerska, to the west of Konjevic Polje. One witness, hidden among trees, saw two or three trucks, followed by an armored vehicle and an earthmoving machine proceeding towards Cerska. After that, he heard gunshots for half an hour and then saw the armoured vehicle going in the opposite direction, but not the earthmoving machine. Other witnesses report seeing a pool of blood alongside the road to Cerska that day. Muhamed Durakovic, a UN translator, probably passed this execution site later that day. He reports seeing bodies tossed into a ditch alongside the road, with some men still alive.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Srebrenica_.E2.80.93_a_.27safe.27_area_.E2.80.93_Part_IV_The_repercussion_and_the_aftermath_until_the_end_of_1995_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Srebrenica_.E2.80.93_a_.27safe.27_area_.E2.80.93_Part_IV_The_repercussion_and_the_aftermath_until_the_end_of_1995-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Aerial photos and excavations later confirmed the presence of a mass grave near this location. Ammunition cartridges found at the scene reveal that the victims were lined up on one side of the road, whereupon their executioners shot from the other. The bodies150 in numberwere covered with earth where they lay. It could later be established that they had been killed by guns. All were men, between the ages of 14 and 50. All but three of the 150 were wearing civilian clothes. Many had their hands tied behind their backs. Nine could later be identified and were indeed on the list of missing persons from Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Late_afternoon_of_13_July:_Kravica">
       Late afternoon of 13 July: Kravica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Late afternoon of 13 July: Kravica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Later that same afternoon, 13 July 1995 executions were also conducted in the largest of four warehouses (farm sheds) owned by the Agricultural Cooperative in Kravica. Between 1,000 and 1,500 men had been captured in fields near Sandii and detained in Sandii Meadow. They were brought to Kravica, either by bus or on foot, the distance being approximately one kilometer. A witness recalls seeing around 200 men, stripped to the waist and with their hands in the air, being forced to run in the direction of Kravica. An aerial photograph taken at 14:00 hours that afternoon shows two buses standing in front of the sheds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At around 18:00 hours, when the men were all being held in the warehouse, VRS soldiers threw in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand_grenades" title="Hand grenades">
       hand grenades
      </a>
      and shot with various weapons, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocket_propelled_grenade" title="Rocket propelled grenade">
       rocket propelled grenades
      </a>
      . In the local area it is said that the mass murder in Kravica was unplanned and started quite spontaneously when one of the warehouse doors suddenly swung open.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Supposedly, there was more killing in and around Kravica and Sandii. Even before the murders in the warehouse, some 200 or 300 men were formed up in ranks near Sandii and then were executed en masse with concentrated machine guns. At Kravica, it seems that the local population had a hand in the killings. Some victims were mutilated and killed with knives. The bodies were taken to Bratunac or simply dumped in the river that runs alongside the road. One witness states that this all took place on 14 July. There were three survivors of the mass murder in the farm sheds at Kravica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Armed guards shot at the men who tried to climb out the windows to escape the massacre. When the shooting stopped, the shed was full of bodies. Another survivor, who was only slightly wounded, reports:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       I was not even able to touch the floor, the concrete floor of the warehouse.... After the shooting, I felt a strange kind of heat, warmth, which was coming from the blood that covered the concrete floor and I was stepping on the dead people who were lying around. But there were even men (just men) who were still alive, who were only wounded and as soon as I would step on him, I would hear him cry, moan, because I was trying to move as fast as I could. I could tell that people had been completely disembodied and I could feel bones of the people that had been hit by those bursts of bullets or shells, I could feel their ribs crushing. Then I would get up again and continue....
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         51
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      When this witness climbed out of a window, he was seen by a guard who shot at him. He then pretended to be dead and managed to escape the following morning. The other witness quoted above spent the night under a heap of bodies; the next morning, he watched as the soldiers examined the corpses for signs of life. The few survivors were forced to sing Serbian songs, and were then shot. Once the final victim had been killed, an excavator was driven in to shunt the bodies out of the shed; the asphalt outside was then hosed down with water. In September 1996, however, it was still possible to find the evidence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Analyses of hair, blood and explosives residue collected at the Kravica Warehouse provide strong evidence of the killings. Experts determined the presence of bullet strikes, explosives residue, bullets and shell cases, as well as human blood, bones and tissue adhering to the walls and floors of the building. Forensic evidence presented by the ICTY Prosecutor established a link between the executions in Kravica and the 'primary' mass grave known as Glogova 2, in which the remains of 139 people were found. In the 'secondary' grave known as Zeleni Jadar 5 there were 145 bodies, a number of which were charred. Pieces of brick and window frame which were found in the Glogova 1 grave that was opened later also established a link with Kravica. Here, the remains of 191 victims were found.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="13.E2.80.9314_July:_Ti.C5.A1.C4.87a">
       1314 July: Tia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: 1314 July: Tia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      As the buses crowded with Bosnian women, children and elderly made their way from Potoari to Kladanj, they were stopped at Tia village, searched, and the Bosnian men and boys found on board were removed from the bus. The evidence reveals a well-organised operation in Tia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From the checkpoint, an officer directed the soldier escorting the witness towards a nearby school where many other prisoners were being held. At the school, a soldier on a field telephone appeared to be transmitting and receiving orders. Sometime around midnight, the witness was loaded onto a truck with 22 other men with their hands tied behind their backs. At one point the truck stopped and a soldier on the scene said: "Not here. Take them up there, where they took people before." The truck reached another stopping point where the soldiers came around to the back of the truck and started shooting the prisoners. The survivor escaped by running away from the truck and hiding in a forest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="14_July:_Grbavci_and_Orahovac">
       14 July: Grbavci and Orahovac
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 14 July: Grbavci and Orahovac">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A large group of the prisoners who had been held overnight in Bratunac were bussed in a convoy of 30 vehicles to the Grbavci school in
      <a href="/wiki/Orahovac" title="Orahovac">
       Orahovac
      </a>
      early in the morning of 14 July 1995. When they got there, the school gym was already half-filled with prisoners who had been arriving since the early morning hours and within a few hours, the building was completely full. Survivors estimated that there were 2,000 to 2,500 men there, some of them very young and some quite elderly, although the ICTY Prosecution suggested this may have been an over-estimation and that the number of prisoners at this site was probably closer to 1,000. Some prisoners were taken outside and killed. At some point, a witness recalled, General Mladi arrived and told the men: "Well, your government does not want you and I have to take care of you."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After being held in the gym for several hours, the men were led out in small groups to the execution fields that afternoon. Each prisoner was blindfolded and given a drink of water as he left the gym. The prisoners were then taken in trucks to the execution fields less than one kilometre away. The men were lined up and shot in the back; those who survived the initial shooting were killed with an extra shot. Two adjacent meadows were used; once one was full of bodies, the executioners moved to the other. While the executions were in progress, the survivors said, earth-moving equipment was digging the graves. A witness who survived the shootings by pretending to be dead, reported that General Mladi drove up in a red car and watched some of the executions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The forensic evidence supports crucial aspects of the survivors' testimony. Both aerial and satellite photos show that the ground in Orahovac was disturbed between 5 and 27 July 1995 and again between 7 and 27 September 1995. Two primary mass graves were uncovered in the area and were named Lazete 1 and Lazete 2 by investigators.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Lazete 1 gravesite was exhumed by the ICTY Prosecution between 13 July and 3 August 2000. All of the 130 individuals uncovered, for whom sex could be determined, were male; 138 blindfolds were uncovered in the grave. Identification material for 23 persons, listed as missing following the fall of Srebrenica, was located during the exhumations at this site. The gravesite Lazete 2 was partly exhumed by a joint team from the Office of the Prosecutor and Physicians for Human Rights between August and September 1996 and completed in 2000. All of the 243 victims associated with Lazete 2 were male and the experts determined that the vast majority died of gunshot injuries. In addition, 147 blindfolds were located.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Forensic analysis of soil/pollen samples, blindfolds, ligatures, shell cases and aerial images of creation/disturbance dates, further revealed that bodies from the Lazete 1 and 2 graves were removed and reburied at secondary graves named Hodii Road 3, 4 and 5. Aerial images show that these secondary gravesites were created between 7 September and 2 October 1995 and all of them were exhumed in 1998.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="14.E2.80.9315_July:_Petkovi.C4.87i">
       1415 July: Petkovii
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 1415 July: Petkovii">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Mass_Gravesite_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Delegates of the International Association of Genocide Scholars (IAGS) examine an exhumed mass grave of victims of the July 1995 Srebrenica massacre, outside the village of Potocari, Bosnia and Herzegovina. July 2007.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 14 and 15 July 1995, another large group of prisoners numbering some 1,500 to 2,000 were taken from Bratunac to the school in Petkovii. The conditions under which these men were held at the Petkovii school were even worse than those in Grabavci. It was hot, overcrowded and there was no food or water. In the absence of anything else, some prisoners chose to drink their own urine. Every now and then, soldiers would enter the room and physically abuse prisoners, or would call them outside.
