A few of the prisoners contemplated an escape attempt, but others said it would be better to stay since the International Red Cross would be sure to monitor the situation and they could not all be killed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The men were called outside in small groups. They were ordered to strip to the waist and to remove their shoes, whereupon their hands were tied behind their backs. During the night of 14 July, the men were taken by truck to the dam at Petkovii. Those who arrived later could see immediately what was happening there. A large number of bodies were strewn on the ground, their hands tied behind their backs. Small groups of five to ten men were taken out of the trucks, lined up and shot. Some begged for water but their pleas were ignored.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A survivor described his feelings of fear combined with thirst thus:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       I was really sorry that I would die thirsty, and I was trying to hide amongst the people as long as I could, like everybody else. I just wanted to live for another second or two. And when it was my turn, I jumped out with what I believe were four other people. I could feel the gravel beneath my feet. It hurt.... I was walking with my head bent down and I wasn't feeling anything.... And then I thought that I would die very fast, that I would not suffer. And I just thought that my mother would never know where I had ended up. This is what I was thinking as I was getting out of the truck. [As the soldiers walked around to kill the survivors of the first round of shooting] I was still very thirsty. But I was sort of between life and death. I didn't know whether I wanted to live or to die anymore. I decided not to call out for them to shoot and kill me, but I was sort of praying to God that they'd come and kill me.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         51
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      After the soldiers had left, two survivors helped each other to untie their hands, and then crawled over the heap of bodies towards the woods, where they intended to hide. As dawn arrived, they could see the execution site where bulldozers were collecting the bodies. On the way to the execution site, one of the survivors had peeked out from under his blindfold and had seen that Mladi was also on his way to the scene.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Aerial photos confirmed that the earth near the Petkovii dam had been disturbed, and that it was disturbed yet again some time between 7 and 27 September 1995. When the grave here was opened in April 1998, there seemed to be many bodies missing. Their removal had been accomplished with mechanical apparatus, causing considerable disturbance to the grave and its contents. At this time, the grave contained the remains of no more than 43 persons. Other bodies had been removed to a secondary grave, Liplje 2, prior to 2 October 1995. Here, the remains of at least 191 individuals were discovered.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY_51-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="14.E2.80.9316_July:_Branjevo">
       1416 July: Branjevo
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: 1416 July: Branjevo">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 14 July 1995 more prisoners from Bratunac were bussed northward to a school in the village of Pilica, north of Zvornik. As at other detention facilities, there was no food or water and several men died in the school gym from heat and dehydration. The men were held at the Pilica school for two nights. On 16 July 1995, following a now familiar pattern, the men were called out of the school and loaded onto buses with their hands tied behind their backs. They were then driven to the Branjevo Military Farm, where groups of 10 were lined up and shot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-233_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-233-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Dra%C5%BEen_Erdemovi%C4%87" title="Draen Erdemovi">
       Draen Erdemovi
      </a>
      who confessed killing at least 70 Bosniakswas a member of the VRS 10th
      <a href="/wiki/Sabotage" title="Sabotage">
       Sabotage
      </a>
      Detachment (a Main Staff subordinate unit) and participated in the mass execution. Erdemovi appeared as a prosecution witness and testified: "The men in front of us were ordered to turn their backs. When those men turned their backs to us, we shot at them. We were given orders to shoot."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-234_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-234-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On this point, one of the survivors recalls:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       When they shot, I threw myself on the ground... one man fell on my head. I think that he was killed on the spot. I could feel the hot blood pouring over me.... I could hear one man crying for help. He was begging them to kill him. And they simply said "Let him suffer. We'll kill him later."
      </p>
      <div class="templatequotecite">
       Witness Q
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         117
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </div>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      Erdemovi said that all but one of the victims wore civilian clothes and that, except for one person who tried to escape, they offered no resistance before being shot. Sometimes the executioners were particularly cruel. When some of the soldiers recognised acquaintances from Srebrenica, they beat and humiliated them before killing them. Erdemovic had to persuade his fellow soldiers to stop using a machine gun for the killings; while it mortally wounded the prisoners it did not cause death immediately and prolonged their suffering.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-234_116-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-234-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between 1,000 and 1,200 men were killed in the course of that day at this execution site.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Aerial photographs, taken on 17 July 1995 of an area around the Branjevo Military Farm, show a large number of bodies lying in the field near the farm, as well as traces of the excavator that collected the bodies from the field.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-237_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-237-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mass_Graves.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="450" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Mass_Graves.jpg/220px-Mass_Graves.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Mass_Graves.jpg/330px-Mass_Graves.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Mass_Graves.jpg/440px-Mass_Graves.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mass_Graves.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Satellite photo of
        <a href="/wiki/Nova_Kasaba" title="Nova Kasaba">
         Nova Kasaba
        </a>
        mass graves.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Erdemovi testified that, at around 15:00 hours on 16 July 1995 after he and his fellow soldiers from the 10th Sabotage Detachment had finished executing the prisoners at the Branjevo Military Farm, they were told that there was a group of 500 Bosnian prisoners from Srebrenica trying to break out of a nearby Dom Kultura club. Erdemovi and the other members of his unit refused to carry out any more killings. They were then told to attend a meeting with a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Colonel" title="Lieutenant Colonel">
       Lieutenant Colonel
      </a>
      at a caf in Pilica. Erdemovi and his fellow-soldiers travelled to the caf as requested and, as they waited, they could hear shots and grenades being detonated. The sounds lasted for approximately 1520 minutes after which a soldier from Bratunac entered the caf to inform those present that "everything was over".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-244_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-244-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There were no survivors to explain exactly what had happened in the Dom Kultura.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-244_120-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-244-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The executions at the Dom Kultura were remarkable in that this was no remote spot but a location in the centre of town on the main road from Zvornik to Bijeljina.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Over a year later, it was still possible to find physical evidence of this crime. As in Kravica, many traces of blood, hair and body tissue were found in the building, with cartridges and shells littered throughout the two storeys.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-245_122-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-245-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It could also be established that explosives and machine guns had been used. Human remains and personal possessions were found under the stage, where blood had dripped down through the floorboards.
     </p>
     <p>
      Two of the three survivors of the executions at the Branjevo Military Farm were arrested by local Bosnian Serb police on 25 July and sent to the
      <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">
       prisoner of war
      </a>
      compound at Batkovici. One had been a member of the group separated from the women in Potoari on 13 July. The prisoners who were taken to Batkovici survived the ordeal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and were later able to testify before the Tribunal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
       <a href="#cite_note-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      anari Road 12 was the site of the re-interment of at least 174 bodies, moved here from the mass grave at the Branjevo Military Farm.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-238_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-238-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Only 43 were complete sets of remains, most of which established that death had taken place as the result of rifle fire. Of the 313 various body parts found, 145 displayed gunshot wounds of a severity likely to prove fatal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning-A4_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manning-A4-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="14.E2.80.9317_July:_Kozluk">
       1417 July: Kozluk
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: 1417 July: Kozluk">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The exact date of the executions at Kozluk is not known, although it can be narrowed down to the period of 14 to 17 July 1995. The most probable dates are 15 and 16 July, not least due to the geographic location of Kozluk, between Petkovii Dam and the Branjevo Military Farm. It therefore falls within the pattern of ever more northerly execution sites: Orahovac on 14 July, Petkovii Dam on 15 July, the Branjevo Military Farm and the Pilica Dom Kultura on 16 July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-253_127-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-253-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another indication is that a Zvornik Brigade excavator spent eight hours in Kozluk on 16 July and a truck belonging to same brigade made two journeys between Orahovac and Kozluk that day. A bulldozer is known to have been active in Kozluk on 18 and 19 July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-252_128-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-252-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Among Bosnian refugees in Germany, there were rumors of executions in
      <a href="/wiki/Kozluk" title="Kozluk">
       Kozluk
      </a>
      , during which the five hundred or so prisoners were forced to sing Serbian songs as they were being transported to the executions site. Although no survivors have since come forward, investigations in 1999 led to the discovery of a mass grave near Kozluk.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-249_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-249-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This proved to be the actual location of an execution as well, and lay alongside the
      <a href="/wiki/Drina" title="Drina">
       Drina
      </a>
      accessible only by driving through the barracks occupied by the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Drina_Wolves&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Drina Wolves (page does not exist)">
       Drina Wolves
      </a>
      , a regular police unit of Republika Srpska. The grave was not dug specifically for the purpose: it had previously been a quarry and a landfill site. Investigators found many shards of green glass which the nearby 'Vitinka' bottling plant had dumped there. This facilitated the process of establishing links with the secondary graves along anari Road.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning-A11_130-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manning-A11-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The grave at Kozluk had been partly cleared some time prior to 27 September 1995 but no fewer than 340 bodies were found there nonetheless.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-250_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-250-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 237 cases, it was clear that they had died as the result of rifle fire: 83 by a single shot to the head, 76 by one shot through the torso region, 72 by multiple bullet wounds, five by wounds to the legs and one person by bullet wounds to the arm. The ages of the victims were between 8 and 85 years old. Some had been physically disabled, occasionally as the result of amputation. Many had clearly been tied and bound using strips of clothing or nylon thread.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning-A11_130-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manning-A11-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Along the anari Road are twelve known mass graves, of which only twoanari Road 3 and 12have been investigated in detail by 2001.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manning-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      anari Road 3 is known to have been a secondary grave linked to Kozluk, as shown by the glass fragments and labels from the Vitinka factory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-251_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-251-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The remains of 158 victims were found here, of which 35 bodies were still more or less intact and indicated that most had been killed by gunfire.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning-p9_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Manning-p9-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="13.E2.80.9318_July:_Bratunac-Konjevi.C4.87_Polje_road">
       1318 July: Bratunac-Konjevi Polje road
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: 1318 July: Bratunac-Konjevi Polje road">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 13 July, near Konjevi Polje, Serb soldiers summarily executed hundreds of Bosniaks, including women and children.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baacbh.org_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-baacbh.org-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The men who were found attempting to escape by the Bratunac-Konjevi Polje road were told that the Geneva Convention would be observed if they gave themselves up.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-63_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-63-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Bratunac, men were told that there were Serbian personnel standing by to escort them to
      <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">
       Zagreb
      </a>
      for an exchange of prisoners. The visible presence of UN uniforms and UN vehicles, stolen from Dutchbat, were intended to contribute to the feeling of reassurance. On 17 to 18 July, Serb soldiers captured about 150200 Bosnians in the vicinity of Konjevic Polje and summarily executed about one-half of them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baacbh.org_135-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-baacbh.org-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="18.E2.80.9319_July:_Nezuk-Baljkovica_frontline">
       1819 July: Nezuk-Baljkovica frontline
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: 1819 July: Nezuk-Baljkovica frontline">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      After the closure of the corridor at Baljkovica, several groups of stragglers nevertheless attempted to escape into Bosnian territory. Most were captured by VRS troops in the NezukBaljkovica area and killed on the spot. In the vicinity of Nezuk, about 20 small groups surrendered to Bosnian Serb military forces. After the men surrendered, Bosnian Serb soldiers ordered them to line up and summarily executed them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3665_100-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3665-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baacbh.org_135-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-baacbh.org-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 19 July, for example, a group of approximately 11 men was killed at Nezuk itself by units of the 16th
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbian_Krajina" title="Republic of Serbian Krajina">
       Krajina
      </a>
      Brigade, then operating under the direct command of the Zvornik Brigade. Reports reveal that a further 13 men, all ARBiH soldiers, were killed at Nezuk on 19 July.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY-IIB5j_137-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY-IIB5j-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The report of the march to Tuzla includes the account of an ARBiH soldier who witnessed several executions carried out by police that day. He survived because 30 ARBiH soldiers were needed for an exchange of prisoners following the ARBiH's capture of a VRS officer at Baljkovica. The soldier was himself exchanged late 1995; at that time, there were still 229 men from Srebrenica in the Batkovici
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war_camp" title="Prisoner of war camp">
       prisoner of war camp
      </a>
      , including two men who had been taken prisoner in 1994.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the same time, RS Ministry of the Interior forces conducting a search of the terrain from Kamenica as far as Snagovo killed eight Bosniaks.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch23_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch23-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Around 200 Muslims armed with
      <a href="/wiki/Automatic_rifle" title="Automatic rifle">
       automatic
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunting_rifle" title="Hunting rifle">
       hunting rifles
      </a>
      were reported to be hiding near the old road near Snagovo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch23_138-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch23-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the morning, about 50 Bosniaks attacked the Zvornik Brigade line in the area of Pandurica, attempting to break through to Bosnian government territory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch23_138-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch23-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Zvornik Public Security Centre planned to surround and destroy these two groups the following day using all available forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
       <a href="#cite_note-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="20.E2.80.9322_July:_Meces_area">
       2022 July: Meces area
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: 2022 July: Meces area">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      According to ICTY indictments of Radovan Karadi and Ratko Mladi, on 20 to 21 July 1995 near the village of Meces, Bosnian Serb military personnel, using megaphones, urged Bosnian men who had fled Srebrenica to surrender and assured them that they would be safe. Approximately 350 men responded to these entreaties and surrendered. Serb soldiers then took approximately 150 of them, instructed them to dig their own graves and summarily executed them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_massacre">
       After the massacre
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: After the massacre">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ICMP-PIP.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ICMP-PIP.jpg/220px-ICMP-PIP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ICMP-PIP.jpg/330px-ICMP-PIP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/ICMP-PIP.jpg/440px-ICMP-PIP.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ICMP-PIP.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        ICMP's
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Podrinje_Identification_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Podrinje Identification Project (page does not exist)">
         Podrinje Identification Project
        </a>
        (PIP) was formed to deal with the identification primarily of victims of 1995 Srebrenica massacre. PIP includes a facility for storing, processing, and handling exhumed remains. Much of the remains are only fragments or commingled body fragments since they were recovered from secondary
        <a href="/wiki/Mass_grave" title="Mass grave">
         mass graves
        </a>
        . The photo depicts one section of the refrigerated
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mortuary" title="Mortuary">
         mortuary
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During the days following the massacre, American
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spy_plane" title="Spy plane">
       spy planes
      </a>
      overflew the area of Srebrenica, and took photos showing the ground in vast areas around the town had been removed, a sign of mass burials.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 22 July, the commanding officer of the
      <a href="/wiki/Zvornik_Brigade" title="Zvornik Brigade">
       Zvornik Brigade
      </a>
      , Lieutenant Colonel
      <a href="/wiki/Vinko_Pandurevi%C4%87" title="Vinko Pandurevi">
       Vinko Pandurevi
      </a>
      , requested the Drina Corps to set up a committee to oversee the exchange of prisoners. He also asked for instructions where the prisoners of war his unit had already captured should be taken and to whom they should be handed over. Approximately 50 wounded captives were taken to the Bratunac hospital. Another group of prisoners was taken to the Batkovii camp (near Bijeljina), and these were mostly exchanged later.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 25 July, the Zvornik Brigade captured 25 more ARBiH soldiers who were taken directly to the camp at Batkovii, as were 34 ARBiH men captured the following day.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Zvornik_Brigade" title="Zvornik Brigade">
       Zvornik Brigade
      </a>
      reports up until 31 July continue to describe the search for refugees and the capture of small groups of Bosniaks.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of Bosniaks managed to cross over the River Drina into Serbia at
      <a href="/wiki/Ljubovija" title="Ljubovija">
       Ljubovija
      </a>
      and Bajina Bata. 38 of them were returned to RS. Some were taken to the Batkovii camp, where they were exchanged. The fate of the majority has not been established.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some of those attempting to cross the Drina drowned.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By 17 July 201 Bosniak soldiers had arrived in
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDepa" title="epa">
       epa
      </a>
      , exhausted and many with light wounds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 28 July another 500 had arrived in epa from Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After 19 July 1995, small Bosniak groups were hiding in the woods for days and months, trying to reach Tuzla.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trial-ch24_141-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-trial-ch24-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Numerous refugees found themselves cut off for some time in the area around Mount Udrc. They did not know what to do next or where to go; they managed to stay alive by eating snails, leaves and mushrooms. The atmosphere was one of tension, hunger and desperation. On or about 23 July, the Bosnian Serbs swept through this area too, and according to one survivor they killed many people as they did so.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Meanwhile, the VRS had commenced the process of clearing the bodies from around Srebrenica, epa, Kamenica and Snagovo. Work parties and municipal services were deployed to help. In Srebrenica, the refuse that had littered the streets since the departure of the people was collected and burnt, the town disinfected and deloused.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Wanderers">
       Wanderers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Wanderers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="262" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section
         <b>
          does not
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
           cite
          </a>
          any
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           references or sources
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please help improve this section by
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">
           adding citations to reliable sources
          </a>
          . Unsourced material may be challenged and
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           removed
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (July 2015)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Many people in the part of the column which had not succeeded in passing Kamenica did not wish to give themselves up and decided to turn back towards epa. Others remained where they were, splitting up into smaller groups of no more than ten. Some wandered around for months, either alone or groups of two, four or six men. Few knew the way and so attempted to navigate by following overhead power cables. They often found corpses, by now in a state of decomposition. Sometimes one group met another group from Srebrenica who knew of a deserted Bosniak village in the region; they would then proceed there together.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some of the Bosniak men decided to retrace their steps towards the Srebrenica region, since this was familiar territory and they knew where to find food. From here, they would once again set out towards epa or attempt to reach Tuzla. Some arrived in Tuzla after many months, having been wandering around the area between Srebrenica and Udrc with absolutely no sense of direction. A few hundred managed to reach epa just before the Serb military, paramilitary and police forces occupied the enclave on 25 July 1995. Once epa had succumbed to the Serb pressure, they had to move on once more, either trying to reach Tuzla or crossing the River Drina into Serbia.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To feed themselves, the men took potatoes and other vegetables from the fields around the Serbian villages at night. The local Serb population therefore began to mount patrols around their villages. The Bosniaks would generally sleep by day and wait for the cover of darkness before moving on. This continued for a long time. For example, the people of Milici, a village on the route to Tuzla, discovered the disappearance of livestock in November 1995 and formed an armed group in search of stragglers from the column.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There are many stories recalling the experiences of those who lost contact with the column, their wanderings and the horrors they saw. One involves three young men aged 17, 18 and 19, who on several occasions attempted to cross the main Konjevi Polje to Nova Kasaba road but were unsuccessful in doing so each time. They eventually managed to reach epa only after the enclave had fallen as well. The group had set up camp in a couple of deserted Bosniak villages where they managed to hide out for several months without attracting attention. Sometimes the teenagers would escort groups of other refugees as far as the next obstacle, before eventually returning to their base. Finally, on 26 April 1996, a full six months after the signing of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dayton_Accord" title="Dayton Accord">
       Dayton Accord
      </a>
      , they crossed the Drina into Serbia.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <b>
       Zvornik 7
      </b>
     </p>
     <p>
      The most famous group of seven men wandered about in occupied territory for the entire winter. On 10 May 1996, after nine months on the run and over six months after the end of the war, they were discovered in a quarry by American
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFOR" title="IFOR">
       IFOR
      </a>
      soldiers. They immediately turned over to the patrol; they were searched and their weapons (two
      <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">
       pistols
      </a>
      and three hand grenades) were confiscated. The men said that they had been in hiding in the immediate vicinity of Srebrenica since the fall of the enclave. They did not look like soldiers and the Americans decided that this was a matter for the police.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The operations officer of this American unit ordered that a Serb patrol should be escorted into the quarry whereupon the men would be handed over to the Serbs.
     </p>
     <p>
      The prisoners said they were initially tortured after the transfer, but later were treated relatively well. In April 1997 the local court in
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      convicted the group, known as the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zvornik_7&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zvornik 7 (page does not exist)">
       Zvornik 7
      </a>
      , for illegal possession of firearms and three of them for the murder of four Serbian woodsmen. When announcing the verdict the presenter of the TV of Republika Srpska described them as
      <i>
       the group of Muslim terrorists from Srebrenica who last year massacred Serb civilians.
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trial was widely condemned by the international community as "a flagrant miscarriage of justice",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the conviction was later quashed for 'procedural reasons' following pressure from the international community. In 1999, the three remaining defendants in the Zvornik 7 case were swapped for three Serbs serving 15 years each in a Bosnian prison.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reburials_in_the_secondary_mass_graves">
       Reburials in the secondary mass graves
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Reburials in the secondary mass graves">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HuseinovicSadik.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="423" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/HuseinovicSadik.jpg/220px-HuseinovicSadik.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/HuseinovicSadik.jpg/330px-HuseinovicSadik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/19/HuseinovicSadik.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HuseinovicSadik.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Grave of a 13-year-old
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      From approximately 1 August 1995 to 1 November 1995, there was an organised effort to remove the bodies from primary mass gravesites and transport them to secondary and tertiary gravesites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
       International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia
      </a>
      court case "Prosecutor v. Blagojevic and Jokic", the trial chamber found that this reburial effort was an attempt to conceal evidence of the mass murders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trial chamber found that the cover up operation was ordered by the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=VRS_Main_Staff&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="VRS Main Staff (page does not exist)">
       VRS Main Staff
      </a>
      and subsequently carried out by members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bratunac" title="Bratunac">
       Bratunac
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zvornik" title="Zvornik">
       Zvornik
      </a>
      Brigades.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
       <a href="#cite_note-149">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The cover-up operation has had a direct impact on the recovery and identification of the remains. The removal and reburial of the bodies have caused them to become dismembered and co-mingled, making it difficult for forensic investigators to positively identify the remains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durnford-BBB_150-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Durnford-BBB-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example, in one specific case, the remains of one person were found in two different locations, 30km apart.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
       <a href="#cite_note-151">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition to the ligatures and blindfolds found at the mass graves, the effort to hide the bodies has been seen as evidence of the organised nature of the massacres and the non-combatant status of the victims, since had the victims died in normal combat operations, there would be no need to hide their remains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Durnford-BBB_150-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Durnford-BBB-150">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
       <a href="#cite_note-152">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_Volunteers_controversy">
       Greek Volunteers controversy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Greek Volunteers controversy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_Volunteer_Guard" title="Greek Volunteer Guard">
       Greek Volunteer Guard
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agence_France_Presse" title="Agence France Presse">
       Agence France Presse
      </a>
      (AFP), a dozen Greek volunteers fought alongside the Serbs at Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
       <a href="#cite_note-153">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They were members of the Greek Volunteer Guard (), or GVG, a contingent of Greek paramilitaries formed at the request of Ratko Mladi as an integral part of the Drina Corps. The Greek volunteers were motivated by the desire to support their "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_church" title="Orthodox church">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      brothers" in battle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiscali.co.uk_154-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tiscali.co.uk-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They raised the Greek flag at Srebrenica after the fall of the town at Mladi's request, to honour "the brave Greeks fighting on our side."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Radovan Karadi subsequently decorated four of them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
       <a href="#cite_note-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smith_157-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-smith-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
       <a href="#cite_note-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005, Greek deputy
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andreas_Andrianopoulos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Andreas Andrianopoulos (page does not exist)">
       Andreas Andrianopoulos
      </a>
      called for an investigation into the role of Greek volunteers in Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Greek Minister of Justice
      <a href="/wiki/Anastasios_Papaligouras" title="Anastasios Papaligouras">
       Anastasios Papaligouras
      </a>
      commissioned an inquiry, which had still not reported as of July 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2009,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stavros_Vitalis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stavros Vitalis (page does not exist)">
       Stavros Vitalis
      </a>
      announced that the volunteers were suing the writer
      <a href="/wiki/Takis_Michas" title="Takis Michas">
       Takis Michas
      </a>
      for libel over allegations in his book
      <i>
       Unholy Alliance
      </i>
      , in which Michas described aspects of the Greek state's tacit support for the Serbs during the Bosnian War. Insisting that the volunteers had simply taken part in what he described as the "re-occupation" of the town, Vitalis acknowledged that he himself was present with senior Serb officers in "all operations" for Srebrenica's re-occupation by the Serbs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balkaninsight.com_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-balkaninsight.com-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Michas notes that the volunteers were treated like heroes and at no point did Greek justice contact them to investigate their knowledge of potential crimes to assist the work of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
       International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia
      </a>
      at The Hague.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_the_massacre">
       Reactions to the massacre
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Reactions to the massacre">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      During the 2 April 2012 "Srebrenica Debate" in Amsterdam, journalist
      <a class="extiw" href="//nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willem_Lust" title="nl:Willem Lust">
       Willem Lust
      </a>
      (who was present in Srebrenica before the massacre), regretted that Serb forces largely kept journalists away: Lust said that "If one or two camera crews had been there... and had filmed in the enclave especially around the Potocari camp... regardless of how far it would have gone I think live images on, say, CNN... because Mladic was very conscious of how the press portrayed events." He also said "Ultimately, it was press reporting that finally convinced the Americans... that it was time to act. After Srebrenica. You know the story of a photo taken near Tuzla by a Croatian photographer... of a woman from Srebrenica who had hung herself. She had lost her husband. She hung herself on a tree. It made the front page of the Washington Post".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vidqt.com_165-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vidqt.com-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      (Lust also said that "
      <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">
       Al Gore
      </a>
      , who was then vice president, went to
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
       Bill Clinton
      </a>
      and said: My daughter is talking about this. When are we going to act? The story goes that Bill Clinton said: It's time to finish this. Then NATO intervened and soon after it was finished."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vidqt.com_165-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-vidqt.com-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      )
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_war">
       End of the war
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: End of the war">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      After the
      <a href="/wiki/Markale_massacres" title="Markale massacres">
       Markale massacre
      </a>
      on 28 August,
      <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
       NATO
      </a>
      launched
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1995_NATO_bombing_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="1995 NATO bombing in Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       a bombing campaign in Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      lasting from 30 August until 20 September. The
      <a href="/wiki/Dayton_Agreement" title="Dayton Agreement">
       Dayton Peace agreement
      </a>
      of November 1995 effectively ended the war.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_developments">
       Post-war developments
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Post-war developments">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1995:_indictment_of_Radovan_Karad.C5.BEi.C4.87_and_Ratko_Mladi.C4.87">
       1995: indictment of Radovan Karadi and Ratko Mladi
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: 1995: indictment of Radovan Karadi and Ratko Mladi">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 16 November 1995 Radovan Karadi, "President of the Republika Srpska" and Ratko Mladi, Commander of the VRS, were indicted by the International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia for their alleged direct responsibility for the war crimes committed in July 1995 against the Bosnian Muslim population of Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daccess-dds-ny.un.org_166-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-daccess-dds-ny.un.org-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1999_UN_Secretary-General.27s_report">
       1999 UN Secretary-General's report
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: 1999 UN Secretary-General's report">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1999, UN Secretary-General Kofi Annan submitted his report on the Fall of Srebrenica. In it, he acknowledged that the international community as a whole had to accept its share of responsibility for its response to the ethnic cleansing campaign that culminated in the murder of some 7,000 unarmed civilians from the town designated by the Security Council as a "safe area."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daccess-dds-ny.un.org_166-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-daccess-dds-ny.un.org-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_167-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2001_French_parliamentary_report">
       2001 French parliamentary report
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: 2001 French parliamentary report">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A report by a committee of the French parliament, published in 2001, concluded that the fall of Srebrenica was "
      <i>
       un chec de la France
      </i>
      ", a failure for France. As a permanent member of the UN Security Council, France carried a great responsibility for the complex of events that eventually led to the fall of the enclave and the mass murder of thousands of Muslims, according to the report. On the evening of 10 July 1995, General Janvier should have approved the repeated requests for air support against the advancing Serbs made by Dutchbat. Moreover, Janvier "underestimated" General Mladi. According to a majority of the committee no evidence was found for the accusation that he and the French president Chirac had promised Mladi not to carry out any more air strikes in exchange for the release of French hostages. Curiously, in an appendix to the report it is also stated that no evidence was found that this promise had
      <i>
       not
      </i>
      been made.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2002_Dutch_government_report">
       2002 Dutch government report
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: 2002 Dutch government report">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Srebrenica massacre led to long-running discussions in the Netherlands. In 1996, the Dutch government asked the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_Institute_for_War_Documentation" title="Netherlands Institute for War Documentation">
       Netherlands Institute for War Documentation
      </a>
      to conduct research into the events before, during and after the fall of Srebrenica. The resulting report was published in 2002
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica:_a_%E2%80%98safe%E2%80%99_area" title="Srebrenica: a safe area">
        Srebrenica: a safe area
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIOD_169-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NIOD-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It concluded that the Dutchbat mission was not well considered and well-nigh impossible. The NIOD report is cited often, but it has not escaped criticism, leading the
      <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_War_and_Peace_Reporting" title="Institute for War and Peace Reporting">
       Institute for War and Peace Reporting
      </a>
      to label the report
      <i>
       controversial
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        170
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      One of the authors of the report claimed some of the sources were "unreliable", only used to support another author's argument.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As a result the Dutch government accepted partial political responsibility for the circumstances in which the massacre happened
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_cabinet_of_Wim_Kok" title="Second cabinet of Wim Kok">
       second cabinet of Wim Kok
      </a>
      resigned in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2002_First_Republika_Srpska_report">
       2002 First Republika Srpska report
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: 2002 First Republika Srpska report">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In September 2002, the Republika Srpska Office of Relations with the ICTY issued the "
      <a href="/wiki/Report_about_Case_Srebrenica" title="Report about Case Srebrenica">
       Report about Case Srebrenica
      </a>
      ". The document, authored by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darko_Trifunovi%C4%87" title="Darko Trifunovi">
       Darko Trifunovi
      </a>
      , was endorsed by many leading Bosnian Serb politicians. It concluded that 1,800 Bosnian Muslim soldiers died during fighting and a further 100 more died as a result of exhaustion. "The number of Muslim soldiers killed by Bosnian Serbs out of personal revenge or lack of knowledge of international law is probably about 100...It is important to uncover the names of the perpetrators in order to accurately and unequivocally establish whether or not these were isolated instances." The report also examined the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass_graves" title="Mass graves">
       mass graves
      </a>
      , claiming that they were made for hygiene reasons, question the legitimacy of the missing person lists and undermine a key witness' mental health and military history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">
       International Crisis Group
      </a>
      and the United Nations condemned the manipulation of their statements in this report.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2003:_Srebrenica_Genocide_Memorial">
       2003: Srebrenica Genocide Memorial
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: 2003: Srebrenica Genocide Memorial">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Wall of names at the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica_Genocide_memorial" title="Srebrenica Genocide memorial">
         Srebrenica Genocide memorial
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 30 September 2003, former US President
      <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
       Bill Clinton
      </a>
      officially opened the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica_Genocide_memorial" title="Srebrenica Genocide memorial">
       Srebrenica Genocide memorial
      </a>
      to honour the victims of the genocide. The total cost of the project was around $5.8million. "We must pay tribute to the innocent lives, many of them children who were snuffed out in what must be called genocidal madness", Clinton said.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2004:_Second_Republika_Srpska_report_and_official_apology">
       2004: Second Republika Srpska report and official apology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: 2004: Second Republika Srpska report and official apology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 2004, the international community's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Representative_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="High Representative in Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       High Representative
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Paddy_Ashdown" title="Paddy Ashdown">
       Paddy Ashdown
      </a>
      had the Government of
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      form a committee to investigate the events. The committee released a report in October 2004 which acknowledged that at least 7,000 men and boys were killed by Bosnian Serb forces, citing a provisional figure of 7,800.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The findings of the committee remain generally disputed by Serb nationalists, who claim it was heavily pressured by the High Representative, given that an earlier RS government report which exonerated the Serbs was dismissed. Nevertheless,
      <a href="/wiki/Dragan_%C4%8Cavi%C4%87" title="Dragan avi">
       Dragan avi
      </a>
      , the president of
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      , acknowledged in a televised address that Serb forces killed several thousand civilians in violation of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">
       international law
      </a>
      , and asserted that Srebrenica was a dark chapter in Serb history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the report, because of "limited time" and to "maximize resources", the commission "accepted the historical background and the facts stated in the second-instance judgment 'Prosecutor vs.
      <a href="/wiki/Radislav_Krsti%C4%87" title="Radislav Krsti">
       Radislav Krsti
      </a>
      ', when the ICTY convicted the accused for 'assisting and supporting genocide' committed in Srebrenica".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 November 2004, the government of Republika Srpska issued an official apology. The statement came after a government review of the Srebrenica committee's report. "The report makes it clear that enormous crimes were committed in the area of Srebrenica in July 1995. The Bosnian Serb Government shares the pain of the families of the Srebrenica victims, is truly sorry and apologises for the tragedy." the Bosnian Serb government said.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_Release_of_Scorpions_massacre_video">
       2005 Release of Scorpions massacre video
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: 2005 Release of Scorpions massacre video">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 2 June 2005, video evidence was introduced at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87_trial" title="Slobodan Miloevi trial">
       Slobodan Miloevi trial
      </a>
      to testify to the involvement of members of police units from Serbia in the Srebrenica massacre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domovina.net_183-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-domovina.net-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The video, the only undestroyed copy of twenty and previously available for rental in the Serbian town of Sid, was obtained and submitted to the ICTY by
      <a href="/wiki/Nata%C5%A1a_Kandi%C4%87" title="Nataa Kandi">
       Nataa Kandi
      </a>
      , director of the Belgrade-based
      <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_Law_Center" title="Humanitarian Law Center">
       Humanitarian Law Center
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publicinternationallaw.org_184-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-publicinternationallaw.org-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The video footage (starting about 2hr 35 min. into the proceedings) shows an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church" title="Orthodox Church">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      priest blessing several members of a Serbian unit known as the "Scorpions." Later these soldiers are shown visibly abusing civilians physically. They were later identified as four minors as young as 16 and two men in their early twenties. The footage then shows the execution of four of the civilians and shows them lying dead in the field. At this point the cameraman expresses disappointment that the camera's battery is almost out. The soldiers then ordered the two remaining captives to take the four dead bodies into a nearby barn, where they were also killed upon completing this task.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domovina.net_183-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-domovina.net-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publicinternationallaw.org_184-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-publicinternationallaw.org-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The video caused public outrage in Serbia. In the days following its showing, the Serbian government arrested some of the former soldiers identified on the video. The event was extensively covered by the newspaper
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Danas_(newspaper)" title="Danas (newspaper)">
        Danas
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">
       radio
      </a>
      and television station
      <a href="/wiki/B92" title="B92">
       B92
      </a>
      . Nura Alispahi, mother of the 16-year-old Azmir Alispahi, saw the execution of her son on television.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        185
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She said that she was already aware of her son's death and said she had been told that his body was burned following the execution; his remains were among those buried in Potoari in 2003.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        186
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
       <a href="#cite_note-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        187
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The executions took place on 16/17 July, in Trnovo, about 30 minutes from the Scorpions' base near Sarajevo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publicinternationallaw.org_184-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-publicinternationallaw.org-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 April 2007, a special war crimes court in Belgrade convicted four former members of the
      <i>
       Scorpions
      </i>
