      of war crimes, treating the killings as an isolated war crime unrelated to the Srebrenica genocide and ignoring the allegations that the Scorpions were acting under the authority of the Serbian Interior Ministry, MUP.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        188
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_U.S._Congress_and_other_resolutions">
       2005 U.S. Congress and other resolutions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: 2005 U.S. Congress and other resolutions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      House of Representatives Resolution: On 27 June 2005, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">
       United States House of Representatives
      </a>
      passed a resolution (H. Res. 199 sponsored by Congressman
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chris_Smith_(politician)" title="Chris Smith (politician)">
       Christopher Smith
      </a>
      and Congressman
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benjamin_Cardin" title="Benjamin Cardin">
       Benjamin Cardin
      </a>
      ) commemorating the 10th anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide. The resolution was passed by an overwhelming majority of 370 to 1, the only one to vote no being
      <a href="/wiki/Ron_Paul" title="Ron Paul">
       Ron Paul
      </a>
      , with 62 absent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        189
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The resolution states that:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       ...the policies of aggression and ethnic cleansing as implemented by Serb forces in Bosnia and Herzegovina from 1992 to 1995 with the direct support of Serbian regime of
       <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Miloevi">
        Slobodan Miloevi
       </a>
       and its followers ultimately led to the displacement of more than 2,000,000 people, an estimated 200,000 killed, tens of thousands raped or otherwise tortured and abused, and the innocent civilians of Sarajevo and other urban centres repeatedly subjected to shelling and sniper attacks; meet the terms defining the crime of genocide in Article 2 of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Prevention_and_Punishment_of_the_Crime_of_Genocide" title="Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide">
        Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide
       </a>
       , created in Paris on 9 December 1948, and entered into force on 12 January 1951.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         190
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      State of Missouri Resolution: On 6 July 2005, State of Missouri passed the resolution recognising the Srebrenica Genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        191
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      City of St. Louis Proclamation: On 11 July 2005, City of St. Louis issued a Proclamation declaring 11 July Srebrenica Remembrance Day in St. Louis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
       <a href="#cite_note-192">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        192
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_Poto.C4.8Dari_Memorial_bomb_plot">
       2005 Potoari Memorial bomb plot
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: 2005 Potoari Memorial bomb plot">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 6 July 2005, Bosnian Serb police found two powerful bombs at the memorial site just days ahead of a ceremony to mark the massacre's 10th anniversary, when 580 identified victims were to be buried during the ceremony and more than 50,000 people, including international politicians and diplomats, were expected to attend. The bombs would have caused widespread loss of life and injury had they exploded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        193
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        194
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_UN_Secretary-General.27s_message_to_the_10th_anniversary_commemoration">
       2005 UN Secretary-General's message to the 10th anniversary commemoration
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: 2005 UN Secretary-General's message to the 10th anniversary commemoration">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In his address to the 10th anniversary commemoration at Potoari, the UN Secretary-General paid tribute to the victims of "a terrible crime  the worst on European soil since the Second World War", on a date "marked as a grim reminder of man's inhumanity to man". He said that the first duty of the international community was to uncover and confront the full truth about what happened, a hard truth for those who serve the United Nations, because great nations failed to respond adequately. There should have been stronger military forces in place, and a stronger will to use them.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg/220px-Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg/330px-Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg/440px-Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boy_at_2006_Srebrenica_funeral.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A boy at a grave during the 2006 funeral of genocide victims
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Blame lay first and foremost with those who planned and carried out the massacre, assisted them, or harboured and continue to harbour them. However the UN also bore its share of responsibility, having made serious errors of judgement, rooted in a philosophy of impartiality and non-violence which, however admirable, was unsuited to the conflict in Bosnia; because of that the tragedy of Srebrenica would haunt the UN's history forever.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rebuilding trust among the peoples of the region could only done by persisting in the struggle for justice, without which there could be no reconciliation, and no peace for the families of the victims, or for society as a whole.
     </p>
     <p>
      The quest for justice remained incomplete while those charged with being the main architects of this massacre  Ratko Mladi and Radovan Karadi  were still at large and had not been made to answer the charges against them before the International Criminal Tribunal. He called on all Bosnians to search for truth and reconciliation.
     </p>
     <p>
      Even while addressing the crimes of the past, the most important obligation was is to prevent such systematic slaughter ever recurring anywhere again. The world had to equip itself to act collectively against genocide, ethnic cleansing and crimes against humanity. The "responsibility to protect" had to be given tangible meaning, not just rhetorical support.
     </p>
     <p>
      He committed the UN helping the people of Bosnia and Herzegovina to rebuild a viable economy and secure a peaceful, prosperous future among the family of nations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_167-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_Perpetrators_named">
       2005 Perpetrators named
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: 2005 Perpetrators named">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 4 October 2005, the Special Bosnian Serb Government Working Group said that 25,083 people were involved in the massacre, including 19,473 members of various Bosnian Serb armed forces that actively gave orders or directly took part in the massacre. They have identified 17,074 by name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISN_195-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ISN-195">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        195
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has also been reported that some 892 of those suspects still hold positions at or are employed by the government of
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      . The names are still held secret.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty_196-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-amnesty-196">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        196
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2006_Discoveries_of_further_mass_graves">
       2006 Discoveries of further mass graves
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: 2006 Discoveries of further mass graves">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Exhumed_Grave_of_Victims_-_Potocari_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Exhumed Grave of Victims 2007.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      By 2006, 42 mass graves have been uncovered around Srebrenica and the specialists believe there are 22 more mass graves. The victims identified number 2,070 while body parts in more than 7,000 bags still await identification.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
       <a href="#cite_note-197">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        197
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 11 August 2006 over 1,000 body parts were exhumed from one of Srebrenica mass graves located in Kamenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
       <a href="#cite_note-198">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        198
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2006_Suppressed_list_of_perpetrators_in_positions_of_authority_published">
       2006 Suppressed list of perpetrators in positions of authority published
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: 2006 Suppressed list of perpetrators in positions of authority published">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 24 August 2006, the Sarajevo daily newspaper
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oslobodjenje" title="Oslobodjenje">
       Oslobodjenje
      </a>
      started publishing a secret list of over 800 Bosnian Serbs who had participated in the Srebrenica massacre and were believed to be still in positions of power at government and municipal level. The names of the 892 individuals concerned were listed among 28,000 Bosnian Serbs reported to have taken part in the massacre by the official Republika Srpska report on Srebrenica. The list had been withheld from publication with the report by the chief prosecutor of the Bosnian War Crimes Chamber, Marinko Jurcevic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
       <a href="#cite_note-199">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        199
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        200
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2006_Dutch_Srebrenica_medal_controversy">
       2006 Dutch Srebrenica medal controversy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: 2006 Dutch Srebrenica medal controversy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In December 2006, the Dutch government awarded the Dutch UN peacekeepers that served in Srebrenica an insignia because they believe they "deserved recognition for their behaviour in difficult circumstances", also noting the limited mandate and the ill-equipped nature of the mission. However, survivors and relatives of the victims condemned the move calling it a "humiliating decision" and responded with protest rallies in The Hague,
      <a href="/wiki/Assen" title="Assen">
       Assen
      </a>
      (where the ceremony took place) and Bosnia's capital Sarajevo.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
       <a href="#cite_note-201">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        201
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2007_Arrest_of_Zdravko_Tolimir">
       2007 Arrest of Zdravko Tolimir
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: 2007 Arrest of Zdravko Tolimir">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="2304" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Women_and_Monument.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Women at the monument for victims of the July 1995 Srebrenica Massacre. At the annual memorial ceremony in Potoari, Bosnia and Herzegovina, 11 July 2007
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 31 May 2007, former Bosnian Serb general
      <a href="/wiki/Zdravko_Tolimir" title="Zdravko Tolimir">
       Zdravko Tolimir
      </a>
      was apprehended by police from Serbia and the Bosnian Serb republic, turned over to NATO forces at the Banja Luka airport where he was read the ICTY indictment and formally arrested. On 1 June 2007 NATO forces conveyed him to Rotterdam where he was turned over to the International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia (ICTY) in The Hague. As of July 2010, Tolimir was being tried by the ICTY on charges of genocide, conspiracy to commit genocide, extermination, persecution and forcible transfer. The indictment accuses Tolimir of participating in the "joint criminal enterprise to remove the Muslim population" from Srebrenica as well as the enclave of Zepa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        202
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        203
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 12 December 2012, Tolimir was convicted of genocide and sentenced to life imprisonment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        204
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2008_Arrest_of_Radovan_Karad.C5.BEi.C4.87">
       2008 Arrest of Radovan Karadi
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: 2008 Arrest of Radovan Karadi">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan Karadi">
       Radovan Karadi
      </a>
      , with similar charges as Zdravko Tolimir, was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrest_of_Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Arrest of Radovan Karadi">
       arrested
      </a>
      in Belgrade on 21 July 2008 (after 13 years on the run) and brought before
      <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">
       Belgrade
      </a>
      's War Crimes Court.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-serbia_captures_205-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-serbia_captures-205">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        205
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was transferred to the ICTY on 30 July 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
       <a href="#cite_note-206">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        206
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of July 2010 Karadi was being tried at the ICTY on 11 charges of genocide, war crimes and crimes against humanity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
       <a href="#cite_note-207">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        207
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
       <a href="#cite_note-208">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        208
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2009_EU_Parliament_resolution">
       2009 EU Parliament resolution
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: 2009 EU Parliament resolution">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 15 January 2009, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_European_Union" title="Parliament of the European Union">
       Parliament of the European Union
      </a>
      voted with overwhelming majority of 556 votes in favour, 9 against and 22 abstentions on a resolution calling for the recognition of 11 July as a day for EU commemoration of the Srebrenica genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
       <a href="#cite_note-209">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        209
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bosnian Serb politicians rejected the resolution, stating that such a commemoration is unacceptable to the
      <a href="/wiki/Republika_Srpska" title="Republika Srpska">
       Republika Srpska
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
       <a href="#cite_note-210">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        210
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_and_2012_Serbia.27s_official_apology">
       2010 and 2012 Serbia's official apology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: 2010 and 2012 Serbia's official apology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In late March 2010,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Serbia" title="National Assembly of Serbia">
       Serbian Parliament
      </a>
      passed a resolution condemning the Srebrenica massacre and apologizing for Serbia not doing more to prevent the tragedy. The motion was passed by a narrow margin with 127 out of 250
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">
       MPs
      </a>
      voting in favor, with 173 legislators present during the vote. The
      <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Party of Serbia">
       Socialist Party of Serbia
      </a>
      , formerly under
      <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Miloevi">
       Slobodan Miloevi
      </a>
      and now under new leadership, voted in favor of adopting the resolution. Opposition parties, in turn, expressed their discontent with the resolution claiming its text was "shameful" for Serbia, either claiming the wording was too strong or too weak.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
       <a href="#cite_note-211">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        211
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some relatives of Bosniak victims were also unhappy with the apology, as it did not use the word 'genocide', but rather pointed at the
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Genocide_case" title="Bosnian Genocide case">
       Bosnian Genocide case
      </a>
      ruling of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
       <a href="#cite_note-212">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        212
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Serbian president,
      <a href="/wiki/Boris_Tadi%C4%87" title="Boris Tadi">
       Boris Tadi
      </a>
      , said that the declaration is the highest expression of patriotism and that it represents distancing from crimes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
       <a href="#cite_note-213">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        213
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Sulejman_Tihi%C4%87" title="Sulejman Tihi">
       Sulejman Tihi
      </a>
      , former Bosniak member of the
      <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      and the current President of the
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Peoples_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="House of Peoples of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       House of Peoples of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      stated that now Bosnia and Herzegovina must adopt a similar resolution condemning crimes against
      <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
       Serbs
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">
       Croats
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
       <a href="#cite_note-214">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        214
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg/220px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg/330px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg/440px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Bosniak mourners at the reburial ceremony for an exhumed victim of the Srebrenica massacre.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 25 April 2013, President
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikolic" title="Tomislav Nikolic">
       Tomislav Nikolic
      </a>
      apologized for the massacre: "I kneel and ask for forgiveness for Serbia for the crime committed in Srebrenica. I apologise for the crimes committed by any individual in the name of our state and our people."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
       <a href="#cite_note-215">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        215
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_Second_Republika_Srpska_report_revision">
       2010 Second Republika Srpska report revision
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: 2010 Second Republika Srpska report revision">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 21 April 2010, the government of
      <a href="/wiki/Milorad_Dodik" title="Milorad Dodik">
       Milorad Dodik
      </a>
      , the prime minister of Republika Srpska, initiated a revision of the 2004 report saying that the numbers of killed were exaggerated and the report was manipulated by a former peace envoy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
       <a href="#cite_note-216">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        216
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_the_High_Representative" title="Office of the High Representative">
       Office of the High Representative
      </a>
      responded and stated that: "The Republika Srpska government should reconsider its conclusions and align itself with the facts and legal requirements and act accordingly, rather than inflicting emotional distress on the survivors, torture history and denigrate the public image of the country".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
       <a href="#cite_note-217">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        217
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 12 July 2010, at the 15th anniversary of the massacre, Milorad Dodik declared that he acknowledges the killings that happened on the site, but does not regard what happened at Srebrenica as
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      , differently from the conclusions of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
       ICTY
      </a>
      and of the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Srebrenica_massacre_.27not_genocide.27_218-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Srebrenica_massacre_.27not_genocide.27-218">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        218
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Russia_vetoes_UN_resolution">
       2015 Russia vetoes UN resolution
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: 2015 Russia vetoes UN resolution">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On July 8, 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
       Russia
      </a>
      vetoed a
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_resolution" title="United Nations Security Council resolution">
       United Nations Security Council resolution
      </a>
      that would have condemned the Srebrenica massacre as a
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Resolution" title="Resolution">
       resolution
      </a>
      was intended to mark the 20th anniversary of the
      <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Killing" title="Killing">
       killing
      </a>
      of 8,000 Muslim men and boys.
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
       Nigeria
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">
       Angola
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
       Venezuela
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abstained" title="Abstained">
       abstained
      </a>
      and the remaining 10 members of the council voted in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Favour" title="Favour">
       favour
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
       <a href="#cite_note-219">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        219
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Lobbied by the Republika Srpska and Serbia, the veto was praised by Serbian President
      <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikoli">
       Tomislav Nikoli
      </a>
      stating that Russia had "prevented an attempt of smearing the entire Serbian nation as genocidal" and proven itself as a true and honest friend.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
       <a href="#cite_note-220">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        220
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="DNA_analysis">
       DNA analysis
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: DNA analysis">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Through the use of
      <a href="/wiki/DNA_profiling" title="DNA profiling">
       DNA profiling
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Missing_Persons" title="International Commission on Missing Persons">
       International Commission on Missing Persons
      </a>
      (ICMP) has revealed the identity of 6,598 persons missing from the July 1995 fall of Srebrenica, by analysing DNA profiles extracted from bone samples of exhumed human remains and matching them to the DNA profiles obtained from blood samples donated by relatives of the missing. The overall high matching rate between DNA extracted from these bone and blood samples leads ICMP to support an estimate of close to 8,100 individuals missing from the fall of Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
       <a href="#cite_note-221">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        221
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_proceedings">
       Legal proceedings
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Legal proceedings">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bosnian_genocide_prosecutions" title="List of Bosnian genocide prosecutions">
       List of Bosnian genocide prosecutions
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia">
       International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:17%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
       <div>
        <p>
         The prosecution proved that genocide was committed in Srebrenica and that General Radislav Krsti, among others, was personally responsible for that.
        </p>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       Olga Kavran, Deputy Coordinator, ICTY Outreach Programme
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
        <a href="#cite_note-222">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         222
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:315px;max-width:315px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:159px;max-width:159px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="393" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg/157px-Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg/236px-Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg/314px-Evstafiev-Radovan_Karadzic_3MAR94.jpg 2x" width="157"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="376" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg/150px-Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg/225px-Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg/300px-Evstafiev-ratko-mladic-1993-w.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="clear:left">
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
        <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan Karadi">
         Radovan Karadi
        </a>
        (left), former president of Republika Srpska, and
        <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87" title="Ratko Mladi">
         Ratko Mladi
        </a>
        (right), former Chief of Staff of the Army of the Republika Srpska are currently under trial.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg/220px-Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg/330px-Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg/440px-Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Front_view_of_the_ICTY.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_Former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia">
         International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Under Resolution 827 (1993) the UN Security Council established the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_Former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia">
       International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia
      </a>
      (ICTY) to try those responsible for violations of international humanitarian law, including genocide, on the territory of the former Yugoslavia
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
       <a href="#cite_note-223">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        223
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Two officers of the Army of the Republika Srpska have been convicted by the Tribunal for their involvement in the Srebrenica genocide,
      <a href="/wiki/Radislav_Krsti%C4%87" title="Radislav Krsti">
       Radislav Krsti
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Vidoje_Blagojevi%C4%87" title="Vidoje Blagojevi">
       Vidoje Blagojevi
      </a>
      . General Krsti, who led the assault on Srebrenica alongside Ratko Mladi, was convicted by the tribunal of aiding and abetting genocide and received a sentence of 35 years imprisonment. Colonel Blagojevi received a sentence of 18 years imprisonment for crimes against humanity. Krsti was the first European to be convicted on a charge of genocide by an international tribunal since the
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">
       Nuremberg trials
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap_224-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ap-224">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        224
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and only the third person ever to have been convicted by an international tribunal under the 1948
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Prevention_and_Punishment_of_the_Crime_of_Genocide" title="Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide">
       Convention on the Prevention and Punishment of the Crime of Genocide
      </a>
      . The ICTY's final ruling was that the Srebrenica massacre was indeed an act of
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTY1_225-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTY1-225">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        225
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Slobodan Miloevi was accused of genocide or complicity in genocide in territories within Bosnia and Herzegovina, including
      <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
       Srebrenica
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
       <a href="#cite_note-226">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        226
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but he died on 11 March 2006 during his ICTY trial and so no verdict was returned.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 10 June 2010, seven senior Serb military and police officers,
      <a href="/wiki/Vujadin_Popovi%C4%87" title="Vujadin Popovi">
       Vujadin Popovi
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ljubi%C5%A1a_Beara" title="Ljubia Beara">
       Ljubia Beara
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Drago_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Drago Nikoli">
       Drago Nikoli
      </a>
      , Ljubomir Borovanin, Vinko Pandurevi, Radivoje Mileti and Milan Gvero, were found guilty of various crimes ranging from genocide to murder and deportation. Popovi and Beara were found guilty of genocide, extermination, murder, and persecution over the genocide, and were sentenced to life in prison. Nikoli was found guilty of aiding and abetting genocide, extermination, murder, and persecution and received 35 years in prison. Borovanin was convicted of aiding and abetting extermination, murder, persecution, forcible transfer, murder as a crime against humanity and as a violation of the laws of customs of war, and was sentenced to 17 years in prison. Mileti was found guilty of murder by majority, persecution, and inhumane acts, specifically forcible transfer, and received 19 years in prison. Gvero was found guilty of persecution and inhumane acts and sentenced to five years in prison, but was acquitted of one count of murder and one count of deportation. Pandurevi was found guilty of aiding and abetting murder, persecution and inhumane acts, but was acquitted of charges of genocide, extermination and deportation, and sentenced to 13 years in prison.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICTYX2_227-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICTYX2-227">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        227
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
       <a href="#cite_note-228">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        228
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 10 September 2010, after the prosecution filed an appeal, Vujadin Popovi, Ljubia Beara, Drago Nikoli, Vinko Pandurevi, Radivoje Mileti and Milan Gvero could face more charges or longer sentences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
       <a href="#cite_note-229">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        229
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2011, the former Chief of the
      <a href="/wiki/Staff_(military)" title="Staff (military)">
       General staff
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Army" title="Yugoslav Army">
       Yugoslav Army
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mom%C4%8Dilo_Peri%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Momilo Perii">
       Momilo Perii
      </a>
      , was sentenced to 27 years in prison for aiding and abetting murder because he provided
      <a href="/wiki/Salary" title="Salary">
       salaries
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">
       ammunition
      </a>
      , staff and
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">
       fuel
      </a>
      to the VRS officers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perisic_Verdict_230-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Perisic_Verdict-230">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        230
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The judges, however, ruled that Perii did not have effective control over Mladi and other VRS officers involved in the crimes. According to the Trial Chamber, the evidence proved Perii's inability to impose binding orders on Mladi.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
       <a href="#cite_note-231">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        231
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 31 May 2007,
      <a href="/wiki/Zdravko_Tolimir" title="Zdravko Tolimir">
       Zdravko Tolimir
      </a>
      , a long time fugitive and a former general in the Army of the Republika Srpska indicted by the Prosecutor of the ICTY on genocide charges in the 199295 Bosnia war was arrested by Serbian and Bosnian police.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
       <a href="#cite_note-232">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        232
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tolimir  "Chemical Zdravko"  is infamous for requesting the use of chemical weapons and proposing military strikes against refugees at Zepa.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
       <a href="#cite_note-233">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        233
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ratko Mladi's deputy in charge of intelligence and security and a key commander at the time of Srebrenica, Tolimir is also believed to be one of the organisers of the support network protecting Mladi and helping him elude justice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
       <a href="#cite_note-234">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        234
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tolimir's trial began on 26 February 2010; he has chosen to represent himself.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
       <a href="#cite_note-235">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        235
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan Karadi">
       Radovan Karadi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87" title="Ratko Mladi">
       Ratko Mladi
      </a>
      have been indicted by the ICTY for genocide and complicity in genocide in several municipalities within Bosnia and Herzegovina, including Srebrenica. Karadi was captured in Serbia on 21 July 2008 and Mladi, on 26 May 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
       <a href="#cite_note-236">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        236
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Karadi declined to enter a plea at his first appearance before the war crimes tribunal on 31 July 2008,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
       <a href="#cite_note-237">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        237
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a formal plea of "not guilty" was then made on his behalf by the judges.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
       <a href="#cite_note-238">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        238
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Karadi insists on defending himself (as he is entitled to under the United Nations court's rules) while at the same time is setting up a team of legal advisers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
       <a href="#cite_note-239">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        239
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Karadi and Mladi, are both on trial on two counts of genocide and other war crimes committed in Srebrenica and also in other districts of Bosnia including Prijedor, Kljuc, Foa, Zvornik and other districts of Bosnia. Karadi and Mladi are charged, separately, with:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
       <a href="#cite_note-240">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        240
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
       <a href="#cite_note-241">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        241
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Count 1: Genocide.
       <ul>
        <li>
         Municipalities:
         <a href="/wiki/Bratunac" title="Bratunac">
          Bratunac
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da" title="Foa">
          Foa
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Klju%C4%8D,_Una-Sana_Canton" title="Klju, Una-Sana Canton">
          Klju
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Kotor_Varo%C5%A1" title="Kotor Varo">
          Kotor Varo
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Prijedor" title="Prijedor">
          Prijedor
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Sanski_Most" title="Sanski Most">
          Sanski Most
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Vlasenica" title="Vlasenica">
          Vlasenica
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Zvornik" title="Zvornik">
          Zvornik
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      To date this count has been dropped from the Prosecutor v. Karadzic trial. To quote the ICTY chamber upon this decision: "The evidence, even if taken at its highest, does not reach a level which a reasonable trier of fact could conclude that genocide occurred in the municipalities of Bosnia and Herzegovina".
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Count 2: Genocide.
       <ul>
        <li>
         Municipality:
         <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
          Srebrenica
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 3: Persecutions on Political, Racial and Religious Grounds, a Crime Against Humanity.
       <ul>
        <li>
         Municipalities:
         <a href="/wiki/Banja_Luka" title="Banja Luka">
          Banja Luka
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Bijeljina" title="Bijeljina">
          Bijeljina
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Bosanska_Krupa" title="Bosanska Krupa">
          Bosanska Krupa
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosanski_Novi" title="Bosanski Novi">
          Bosanski Novi
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Bratunac" title="Bratunac">
          Bratunac
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Br%C4%8Dko_(town)" title="Brko (town)">
          Brko
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Fo%C4%8Da" title="Foa">
          Foa
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Had%C5%BEi%C4%87i" title="Hadii">
          Hadii
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Ilid%C5%BEa" title="Ilida">
          Ilida
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Kalinovik" title="Kalinovik">
          Kalinovik
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Klju%C4%8D,_Una-Sana_Canton" title="Klju, Una-Sana Canton">
          Klju
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Kotor_Varo%C5%A1" title="Kotor Varo">
          Kotor Varo
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Novi_Grad,_Bosanska_Krajina" title="Novi Grad, Bosanska Krajina">
          Novi Grad
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Novo_Sarajevo" title="Novo Sarajevo">
          Novo Sarajevo
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Pale,_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Pale, Bosnia and Herzegovina">
          Pale
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Prijedor" title="Prijedor">
          Prijedor
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Rogatica" title="Rogatica">
          Rogatica
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Sanski_Most" title="Sanski Most">
          Sanski Most
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Sokolac" title="Sokolac">
          Sokolac
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Trnovo,_Republika_Srpska" title="Trnovo, Republika Srpska">
          Trnovo
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Vlasenica" title="Vlasenica">
          Vlasenica
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Vogo%C5%A1%C4%87a" title="Vogoa">
          Vogoa
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Zvornik" title="Zvornik">
          Zvornik
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
          Srebrenica
         </a>
         .
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 4: Extermination, a Crime Against Humanity.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 5: Murder, a Crime Against Humanity.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 6: Murder, a Violation of the Laws or Customs of War.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 7: Deportation, a Crime Against Humanity.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 8: Inhumane Acts (forcible transfer), a Crime Against Humanity.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 9: Acts of Violence the Primary Purpose of which is to Spread Terror among the Civilian Population, a Violation of the Laws or Customs of War.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 10: Unlawful Attacks on Civilians, a Violation of the Laws or Customs of War.
      </li>
      <li>
       Count 11: Taking of Hostages, a Violation of the Laws or Customs of War.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="International_Court_of_Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: International Court of Justice">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Genocide_case" title="Bosnian Genocide case">
       Bosnian Genocide case
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In addition, the Srebrenica massacre was the core issue of the landmark court case
      <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_Genocide" title="Bosnian Genocide">
       Bosnian Genocide
      </a>
      case at the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </a>
      through which Bosnia and Herzegovina accused
      <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">
       Serbia and Montenegro
      </a>
      of genocide. The ICJ presented its judgement on 26 February 2007. It cleared Serbia of direct involvement in
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      during the Bosnian war,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
       <a href="#cite_note-242">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        242
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but ruled that Belgrade did breach international law by failing to prevent the 1995 Srebrenica genocide, and for failing to try or transfer the persons accused of genocide to the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">
       ICTY
      </a>
      , in order to comply with its obligations under Articles I and VI of the Genocide Convention, in particular in respect of General
      <a href="/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87" title="Ratko Mladi">
       Ratko Mladi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICJ-2007-02-26_243-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ICJ-2007-02-26-243">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        243
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
       <a href="#cite_note-244">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        244
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NyTimes-BosniaGenocide_245-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NyTimes-BosniaGenocide-245">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        245
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Citing national security, Serbia obtained permission from the ICTY to keep parts of its military archives out of the public eye during its trial of Slobodan Milosevic, which may have decisively affected the ICJ's judgement in the lawsuit brought against Serbia by Bosnia-Herzegovina, as the archives were hence not on the ICTY's public record  although the ICJ could have, but did not, subpoena the documents themselves.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
       <a href="#cite_note-246">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        246
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Chief prosecutor's office, OTP, rejects allegations that there was a deal with Belgrade to conceal documents from the ICJ Bosnia genocide case.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
       <a href="#cite_note-247">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        247
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="National_courts">
       National courts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: National courts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">
       Serbia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Serbia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <i>
        See also above
        <a href="#2005_Release_of_Scorpions_massacre_video">
         2005 Release of Scorpions massacre video
        </a>
       </i>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      On 10 April 2007, a Serbian war crimes court sentenced four members of a paramilitary group known as the Scorpions to a total of 58 years in prison for the execution of six Bosniaks during the Srebrenica massacre of July 1995.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
       <a href="#cite_note-248">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        248
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">
       Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      On 11 June 2007, the ICTY transferred
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milorad_Trbic" title="Milorad Trbic">
       Milorad Trbic
      </a>
      (former Chief of Security of the Zvornik Brigade of the Army of Republika Srpska) to
      <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">
       Sarajevo
      </a>
      to stand trial for genocide for his actions in and around Srebrenica before the
      <i>
       War Crimes Chamber
      </i>
      (Section I for War Crimes of the Criminal Division of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Court_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="State Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina">
       Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina
      </a>
      ; henceforth: the Court).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249">
       <a href="#cite_note-249">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        249
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Milorad Trbic  "[Is]charged with Genocide pursuant to Article 171 of the Criminal Code of Bosnia and Herzegovina (CC BiH).  The trial commenced on 8 November 2007, and the Prosecutor is currently presenting his evidence."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
       <a href="#cite_note-250">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        250
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The "Mitrovi and others case ("Kravice")" was an important trial before the Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina. The accused "according to the indictment, in the period from 10 to 19 July 1995, as knowing participants in a joint criminal enterprise, the accused committed the criminal offence of genocide. This crime was allegedly committed as part of widespread and systematic attack against the Bosniak population inside the UN protected area of Srebrenica carried out by the Republika Srpska Army (RSA) and the RS Ministry of Interior, with a common plan to annihilate in part a group of Bosniak people."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mitrovic_-Kravice_251-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mitrovic_-Kravice-251">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        251
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 29 July 2008, after a two-year trial, the Court found seven men guilty of genocide for their role in the Srebrenica massacre including the deaths of 1000 Bosniak men in a single day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-2008-07-29_252-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AP-2008-07-29-252">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        252
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-2008-07-29_253-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC-2008-07-29-253">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        253
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The court found that Bosniak men trying to escape from Srebrenica had been told they would be kept safe if they surrendered. Instead, they were transported to an agricultural
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-operative" title="Co-operative">
       co-operative
      </a>
      in the village of
      <a href="/wiki/Kravica" title="Kravica">
       Kravica
      </a>
      , and later executed
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En_masse" title="En masse">
        en masse
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-2008-07-29_252-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-AP-2008-07-29-252">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        252
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-2008-07-29_253-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC-2008-07-29-253">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        253
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 20 April 2010, Croatia arrested Franc Kos, a member of the 10th commando detachment of the Army of the Republika Srpska, over genocide charges for the Srebrenica massacre. Bosnia and Herzegovina has an international warrant out for his arrest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254">
       <a href="#cite_note-254">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        254
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is currently awaiting trial.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birn_255-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-birn-255">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        255
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 29 April 2010, the United States extradited Marko Boki on suspicions of having committed genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBiH_256-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TBiH-256">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        256
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He later plead guilty.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birn_255-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-birn-255">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        255
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 18 January 2011, Israel arrested Aleksandar Cvetkovi, a veteran of the Bosnian Serb Army, after the Bosnian government filed an extradition request. Cvetkovi had moved to Israel in 2006 and secured citizenship through marriage to an Israeli. He was accused of having personally taken part in the executions of more than 800 men and boys, and initiated use of machine guns to speed up the killings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn18012011_257-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnn18012011-257">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        257
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
       <a href="#cite_note-258">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        258
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
       <a href="#cite_note-259">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        259
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 1 August 2011, a Jerusalem court approved Cvetkovi's extradition,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
       <a href="#cite_note-260">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        260
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and an appeal was denied in November 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
       <a href="#cite_note-261">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        261
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Boidar Kuvelja, a former Bosnian Serb policeman, was arrested in
      <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cajni%C4%8De" title="ajnie">
       ajnie
      </a>
      , Bosnia and Herzegovina.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birn18012011_262-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-birn18012011-262">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        262
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
       <a href="#cite_note-263">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        263
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <dl>

     <dl>
      <dt>
       Guilty of aiding and abetting genocide
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Duko Jevi (deputy commander of the interior ministry special police brigade and the commander of the Jahorina special police training center)  found guilty, sentenced to 35 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euronews_25_May_2012_267-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Euronews_25_May_2012-267">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         267
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Mendeljev uri (commander of Jahorina special police training center's first company)  found guilty, sentenced to 30 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euronews_25_May_2012_267-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Euronews_25_May_2012-267">
         <span>

         </span>
