     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">
       Netherlands
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Netherlands">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Survivors and victims' relatives have sought to establish the responsibility of the State of the Netherlands and the United Nations for what happened at Srebrenica in civil law actions brought before The Hague District Court in the Netherlands.
     </p>
     <p>
      In one case the Dutch law firm
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Van_Diepen_Van_der_Kroef&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Van Diepen Van der Kroef (page does not exist)">
       Van Diepen Van der Kroef
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.vandiepen.com_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-www.vandiepen.com-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274">
       <a href="#cite_note-274">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        274
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is representing 11 plaintiffs including the organisation "Mothers of the Enclaves of Srebrenica and epa" (which represents 6,000 relatives of the victims
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275">
       <a href="#cite_note-275">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        275
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ), who asked the court, among other things, to rule that the UN and the State of the Netherlands breached their obligation to prevent
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      , as laid down in the
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Convention" title="Genocide Convention">
       Genocide Convention
      </a>
      and hold them jointly liable to pay compensation for the loss and injury suffered by the plaintiffs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276">
       <a href="#cite_note-276">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        276
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 10 July 2008, the court ruled that it had no jurisdiction against the UN; however, the court is set to rule against the State of the Netherlands
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277">
       <a href="#cite_note-277">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        277
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278">
       <a href="#cite_note-278">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        278
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Plaintiffs have appealed the judgement (in relation to UN immunity).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279">
       <a href="#cite_note-279">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        279
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The second action combined two cases by a former UN interpreter
      <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Nuhanovi%C4%87" title="Hasan Nuhanovi">
       Hasan Nuhanovi
      </a>
      and the family of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rizo_Mustafi%C4%87&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rizo Mustafi (page does not exist)">
       Rizo Mustafi
      </a>
      , an electrician employed by the UN at Srebrenica. They claimed that Dutch troops in the peacekeeping contingent responsible for security in the UN-protected zone allowed
      <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska" title="Army of Republika Srpska">
       VRS
      </a>
      troops to kill their relatives, Nuhanovi's entire immediate family (brother, father and mother)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280">
       <a href="#cite_note-280">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        280
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the Mustafi family's husband and father.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haguejusticeportal.net_281-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-haguejusticeportal.net-281">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        281
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They argued that the Dutch Government (Minister of Defence and Minister of Foreign Affairs) had
      <i>
       de facto
      </i>
      operational command of the Dutch battalion in accordance with the
      <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Netherlands" title="Constitution of the Netherlands">
       Dutch Constitution
      </a>
      (Article 97(2)), which grants the government superior command (
      <i>
       oppergezag
      </i>
      ) over military forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haguejusticeportal.net_281-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-haguejusticeportal.net-281">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        281
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 10 September 2008, the district court dismissed these claims and held that the State could not be held responsible because the Dutchbat peacekeepers were operating in Bosnia under a United Nations mandate and operational command and control over the troops had been transferred to the UN command.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282">
       <a href="#cite_note-282">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        282
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 5 July 2011, the court of appeal reversed and held that the State was responsible for, and indeed actively coordinated, the evacuation once Srebrenica fell, and therefore is responsible for the decision to dismiss Nuhanovi's brother and Mustafi from the Dutchbat compound. The court further held that this decision was wrong, because the Dutch soldiers should have known that they were in great danger of being tortured or killed. Both claimants are therefore eligible for compensation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283">
       <a href="#cite_note-283">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        283
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 6 September 2013, the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Netherlands" title="Supreme Court of the Netherlands">
       Supreme Court
      </a>
      dismissed the Government's appeal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284">
       <a href="#cite_note-284">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        284
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Dutch Government acknowledged the judgment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285">
       <a href="#cite_note-285">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        285
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 16 July 2014, a Dutch court held the Netherlands liable for the killings of more than 300 Bosniaks at Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286">
       <a href="#cite_note-286">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        286
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2015 a Dutch court ruled that the Netherlands are not liable for deaths in Srebrenica.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Analyses">
       Analyses
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Analyses">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Meron" title="Theodor Meron">
       Theodor Meron
      </a>
      , the presiding judge of the Appeals Chamber, stated:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       By seeking to eliminate a part of the Bosnian Muslims, the Bosnian Serb forces committed genocide. They targeted for extinction the 40,000 Bosnian Muslims living in Srebrenica, a group which was emblematic of the Bosnian Muslims in general. They stripped all the male Muslim prisoners, military and civilian, elderly and young, of their personal belongings and identification, and deliberately and methodically killed them solely on the basis of their identity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287">
        <a href="#cite_note-287">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         287
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      In February 2007 the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
       International Court of Justice
      </a>
      (ICJ) concurred with the ICTY judgement, stating:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       The Court concludes that the acts committed at Srebrenica falling within Article II
       <i>
        (a)
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        (b)
       </i>
       of the Convention were committed with the specific intent to destroy in part the group of the Muslims of Bosnia and Herzegovina as such; and accordingly that these were acts of genocide, committed by members of the VRS in and around Srebrenica from about 13 July 1995.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288">
        <a href="#cite_note-288">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         288
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      According to the UK-based Bosnian Institute:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       To say that genocide took place 'only' in Srebrenica in July 1995 flies in the face of earlier judicial rulings. Four international judgments in the especially well-argued cases of Nikola Jorgic, Novislav Djajic, Djuradj Kusljic, and Maksim Sokolovic clearly confirm that genocide took place in several municipalities outside of Srebrenica in 1992. All four trials were conducted in Germany  at the request of the International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia (ICTY)  to ease the caseload of ongoing trials at The Hague. All the relevant appeals have long been exhausted, so that judgments in these cases are final and binding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289">
        <a href="#cite_note-289">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         289
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_Bosnian_forces_on_the_ground">
       Role of Bosnian forces on the ground
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Role of Bosnian forces on the ground">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In response to the suggestion that the Bosniak forces in Srebrenica made no adequate attempt to defend the town, the Report of the Secretary-General pursuant to General Assembly resolution 53/35The Fall of Srebrenica,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290">
       <a href="#cite_note-290">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        290
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      delivered to the 54th session of the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">
       United Nations General Assembly
      </a>
      on 15 November 1999 states:
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       "Concerning the accusation that the Bosniaks did not do enough to defend Srebrenica, military experts consulted in connection with this report were largely in agreement that the Bosniaks could not have defended Srebrenica for long in the face of a concerted attack supported by armour and artillery."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291">
        <a href="#cite_note-291">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         291
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       "Many have accused the Bosniak forces of withdrawing from the enclave as the Serb forces advanced on the day of its fall. However, it must be remembered that on the eve of the final Serb assault the Dutchbat Commander urged the Bosniaks to withdraw from defensive positions south of Srebrenica townthe direction from which the Serbs were advancing. He did so because he believed that NATO aircraft would soon be launching widespread air strikes against the advancing Serbs."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292">
        <a href="#cite_note-292">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         292
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       "A third accusation levelled at the Bosniak defenders of Srebrenica is that they provoked the Serb offensive by attacking out of that safe area. Even though this accusation is often repeated by international sources, there is no credible evidence to support it. Dutchbat personnel on the ground at the time assessed that the few "raids" the Bosniaks mounted out of Srebrenica were of little or no military significance. These raids were often organised in order to gather food, as the Serbs had refused access for humanitarian convoys into the enclave. Even Serb sources approached in the context of this report acknowledged that the Bosniak forces in Srebrenica posed no significant military threat to them. The biggest attack the Bosniaks launched out of Srebrenica during the more than two years during which it was designated a safe area appears to have been the raid on the village of Vinjica, on 26 June 1995, in which several houses were burned, up to four Serbs were killed and approximately 100 sheep were stolen. In contrast, the Serbs overran the enclave two weeks later, driving tens of thousands from their homes, and summarily executing thousands of men and boys. The Serbs repeatedly exaggerated the extent of the raids out of Srebrenica as a pretext for the prosecution of a central war aim: to create a geographically contiguous and ethnically pure territory along the Drina, while freeing their troops to fight in other parts of the country. The extent to which this pretext was accepted at face value by international actors and observers reflected the prism of "moral equivalency" through which the conflict in Bosnia was viewed by too many for too long."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293">
        <a href="#cite_note-293">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         293
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_regarding_Serb_casualties_around_Srebrenica">
       Dispute regarding Serb casualties around Srebrenica
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Dispute regarding Serb casualties around Srebrenica">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      It is agreed by all sides that Serbs suffered a number of casualties during military forays led by
      <a href="/wiki/Naser_Ori%C4%87" title="Naser Ori">
       Naser Ori
      </a>
      . The controversy over the nature and number of the casualties came to a head in 2005, the 10th anniversary of the massacre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw-oric_294-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hrw-oric-294">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        294
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">
       Human Rights Watch
      </a>
      , the ultra-nationalist
      <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Radical_Party" title="Serbian Radical Party">
       Serbian Radical Party
      </a>
      "launched an aggressive campaign to prove that Muslims had committed crimes against thousands of Serbs in the area" which "was intended to diminish the significance of the July 1995 crime."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw-oric_294-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-hrw-oric-294">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        294
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A press briefing by the ICTY Office of the Prosecutor (OTP) dated 6 July 2005 noted that the number of Serb deaths in the region alleged by the Serbian authorities had increased from 1,400 to 3,500, a figure the OTP stated "[does] not reflect the reality."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty-july05_295-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty-july05-295">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        295
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The briefing cited previous accounts:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The Republika Srpska's Commission for War Crimes gave the number of Serb victims in the municipalities of Bratunac, Srebrenica and Skelani as 995; 520 in Bratunac and 475 in Srebrenica.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        The Chronicle of Our Graves
       </i>
       by Milivoje Ivanievi, president of the Belgrade Centre for Investigating Crimes Committed against the Serbs, estimates the number of people killed at around 1,200.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        For the Honourable Cross and Golden Freedom
       </i>
       , a book published by the RS
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior" title="Ministry of Interior">
        Ministry of Interior
       </a>
       , referred to 641 Serb victims in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bratunac" title="Bratunac">
        Bratunac
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
        Srebrenica
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/Skelani" title="Skelani">
        Skelani
       </a>
       region.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      The accuracy of these numbers is challenged: the OTP noted that although Ivanievi's book estimated that around 1,200 Serbs were killed, personal details were only available for 624 victims.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty-july05_295-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty-july05-295">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        295
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The validity of labeling some of the casualties as "victims" is also contested:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty-july05_295-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty-july05-295">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        295
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      studies have found a significant majority of military casualties compared to civilian casualties.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RDC_296-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RDC-296">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        296
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is in line with the nature of the conflictSerb casualties died in raids by Bosniak forces on outlying villages used as military outposts for attacks on Srebrenica
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297">
       <a href="#cite_note-297">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        297
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (many of which had been ethnically cleansed of their Bosniak majority population in 1992).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298">
       <a href="#cite_note-298">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        298
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For example the village of Kravica was attacked by Bosniak forces on
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
       Orthodox
      </a>
      Christmas Day, 7 January 1993. Some Serb sources such as Ivanievi allege that the village's 353 inhabitants were "virtually completely destroyed".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icty-july05_295-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-icty-july05-295">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        295
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In fact, the VRS' own internal records state that 46 Serbs died in the Kravica attack: 35 soldiers and 11 civilians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299">
       <a href="#cite_note-299">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        299
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while the ICTY Prosecutor's Office's investigation of casualties on 7 and 8 January in Kravica and the surrounding villages found that 43 people were killed, of whom 13 were obviously civilians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300">
       <a href="#cite_note-300">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        300
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless the event continues to be cited by Serb sources as the key example of heinous crimes committed by Bosniak forces around Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw-oric_294-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-hrw-oric-294">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        294
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As for the destruction and casualties in the villages of Kravica, Siljkovii, Bjelovac, Fakovii and Sikiri, the judgement states that the prosecution failed to present convincing evidence that the Bosnian forces were responsible for them, because the Serb forces used artillery in the fighting in those villages. In the case of the village of Bjelovac, Serbs even used warplanes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301">
       <a href="#cite_note-301">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        301
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The most up-to-date analysis of Serb casualties in the region comes from the
      <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">
       Sarajevo
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Research_and_Documentation_Center_in_Sarajevo" title="Research and Documentation Center in Sarajevo">
       Research and Documentation Centre
      </a>
      , a non-partisan institution with a multiethnic staff, whose data have been collected, processed, checked, compared and evaluated by international team of experts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RDC_296-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RDC-296">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        296
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302">
       <a href="#cite_note-302">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        302
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303">
       <a href="#cite_note-303">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        303
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The RDC's extensive review of casualty data found that Serb casualties in the Bratunac municipality amounted to 119 civilians and 424 soldiers. It also established that although the 383 Serb victims buried in the Bratunac military cemetery are presented as casualties of ARBiH units from Srebrenica, 139 (more than one third of the total) had fought and died elsewhere in Bosnia and Herzegovina.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RDC_296-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-RDC-296">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        296
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Serb sources maintain that casualties and losses during the period prior to the creation of the safe area gave rise to Serb demands for revenge against the Bosniaks based in Srebrenica. The ARBiH raids are presented as a key motivating factor for the July 1995 genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304">
       <a href="#cite_note-304">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        304
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This view is echoed by international sources including the 2002 report commissioned by the Dutch government on events leading to the fall of Srebrenica (the NIOD report).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIOD-Appendix-IV_305-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NIOD-Appendix-IV-305">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        305
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However these sources also cite misleading figures for the number of Serb casualties in the region.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The efforts to explain the Srebrenica massacre as motivated by revenge have been dismissed as bad faith attempts to justify the genocide.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306">
       <a href="#cite_note-306">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        306
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ICTY Outreach Programme notes that the claim that Bosnian Serb forces killed the prisoners from Srebrenica in revenge for crimes committed by Bosnian Muslim forces against Serbs in the villages around Srebrenica provides no defence under international law and soldiers, certainly experienced officers, would be aware of the fact. To offer revenge as a justification for crimes is to attack the rule of law, and civilization itself, and nor does revenge provide moral justification for killing people simply because they share the same ethnicity as others who perpetrated crimes. The methodical planning and mobilization of the substantial resources involved required orders to be given at a high command level. The VRS had a plan to kill the Bosnian Muslim prisoners, as Dragan Obrenovi confirmed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307">
       <a href="#cite_note-307">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        307
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      To quote the Report of the UN Secretary-General on the Fall of Srebrenica:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308">
       <a href="#cite_note-308">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        308
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <blockquote class="templatequote">
      <p>
       Even though this accusation is often repeated by international sources, there is no credible evidence to support it... The Serbs repeatedly exaggerated the extent of the raids out of Srebrenica as a pretext for the prosecution of a central war aim: to create a geographically contiguous and ethnically pure territory along the Drina, while freeing their troops to fight in other parts of the country. The extent to which this pretext was accepted at face value by international actors and observers reflected the prism of 'moral equivalency' through which the conflict in Bosnia was viewed by too many for too long.
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Claim_that_the_planning_of_mass_executions_in_Srebrenica_defies_military_logic">
       Claim that the planning of mass executions in Srebrenica defies military logic
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Claim that the planning of mass executions in Srebrenica defies military logic">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During
      <a href="/wiki/Radislav_Krsti%C4%87" title="Radislav Krsti">
       Radislav Krsti
      </a>
      's trial before the ICTY, the prosecution's
      <a href="/wiki/Military_advisor" title="Military advisor">
       military advisor
      </a>
      , Richard Butler, pointed out that by carrying out a mass execution, the Serb Army deprived themselves of an extremely valuable bargaining counter. Butler suggested that they would have had far more to gain had they taken the men in Potoari as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" title="Prisoners of war">
       prisoners of war
      </a>
      , under the supervision of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross" title="International Red Cross">
       International Red Cross
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">
       ICRC
      </a>
      ) and the UN troops still in the area. It might then have been possible to enter into some sort of exchange deal or they might have been able to force
      <a href="/wiki/Concession_(politics)" title="Concession (politics)">
       political concessions
      </a>
      . Based on this reasoning, the ensuing mass murder defied military explanation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-un.org_61-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-un.org-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Dutchbat">
       Dutchbat
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Dutchbat">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Dutch Battalion "
      <a href="/wiki/Dutchbat" title="Dutchbat">
       Dutchbat
      </a>
      " has been found guilty
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="what charge? (July 2015)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      by the courts in the Netherlands for failure to protect some of the Bosniak refugees in the Safe Area
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309">
       <a href="#cite_note-309">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        309
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Minister Voohoeve of the Netherlands had ordered that under no circumstances was Dutchbat allowed to cooperate in the separate treatment of men.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310">
       <a href="#cite_note-310">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        310
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A NATO battalion is expected to be able to exercise judgement when confronted with a conflict between rules of engagement and a specific order designed to protect refugees; moreover, it was the Netherlands and not the UN that had effective control of Dutchbat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311">
       <a href="#cite_note-311">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        311
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 13 July, "Dutchbat" expelled
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="(July 2015)">
          why?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      five Bosniak refugees from the United Nations compound. Later proceedings in Dutch courts have established legal liability of The Netherlands for the deaths of those expelled.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2013 the Dutch Supreme Court held the Netherlands responsible for the death of 3 Bosnian men who were expelled from a compound held by "Dutchbat, on 13 July 1995.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT9613_66-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT9613-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Claims_of_problems_in_the_UNPROFOR_chain_of_command_above_.22Dutchbat.22">
       Claims of problems in the UNPROFOR chain of command above "Dutchbat"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title='Edit section: Claims of problems in the UNPROFOR chain of command above "Dutchbat"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brigadier_General" title="Brigadier General">
       Brigadier General
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hagrup_Haukland" title="Hagrup Haukland">
       Hagrup Haukland
      </a>
      was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNPROFOR" title="UNPROFOR">
       UNPROFOR
      </a>
      's Commander of
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312">
       <a href="#cite_note-312">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        312
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the sector in which the killings of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica_Massacre" title="Srebrenica Massacre">
       Srebrenica Massacre
      </a>
      started on 11 July 1995. At this time he was on vacation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vg.no_313-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vg.no-313">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        313
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His subordinate, Colonel
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Charles_Brantz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Charles Brantz (page does not exist)">
       Charles Brantz
      </a>
      phoned Haukland twice on July 9, 1995 to inform about the crisis in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica_Massacre" title="Srebrenica Massacre">
       Srebrenica
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eraker_314-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Eraker-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Confusion within his staff has been attributed in part to his being slow
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vg.no_313-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-vg.no-313">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        313
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to return to his place of work, not arriving at
      <a href="/wiki/Tuzla" title="Tuzla">
       Tuzla
      </a>
      headquarters until July 14.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eraker_314-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Eraker-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Other problems within Haukland's staff included
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eraker_314-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Eraker-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      problems of cooperation between "the
      <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
       Dutch
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani" title="Pakistani">
       Pakistanis
      </a>
      ", according to Harald Valved (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNPROFOR" title="UNPROFOR">
       UNPROFOR
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Military_advisor" title="Military advisor">
       military advisor
      </a>
      ). The report
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica:_a_%E2%80%98safe%E2%80%99_area" title="Srebrenica: a safe area">
        Srebrenica: a safe area
       </a>
      </i>
      says that "The cadres consisted of clans of Norwegian, Pakistani and Dutch military that were incapable of adequate mutual cooperation."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315">
       <a href="#cite_note-315">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        315
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005 an unnamed officer on Haukland's multinational staff at Tuzla in 1995, disputed the claim by Haukland and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_of_Defence_of_Norway" title="Chief of Defence of Norway">
       Chief of Defence
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Arne_Solli" title="Arne Solli">
       Arne Solli
      </a>
      that the attack on Srebrenica was a surprise.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eraker_314-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Eraker-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The officer said "We knew early that the Serbs were amassing their forces around Srebrenica. At the end of June, Haukland informed the headquarters at
      <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">
       Sarajevo
      </a>
      again and again in regards to this".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eraker_314-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Eraker-314">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        314
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2006 media said that "Haukland regularly informed Chief of Defence Arne Sollie about the conditions within Haukland's sector. When Haukland departed Bosnia on his vacation to Norway, he travelled on the same airplane as the defence minister".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Airplane_316-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Airplane-316">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        316
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A 2002 report by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_Institute_for_War_Documentation" title="Netherlands Institute for War Documentation">
       Netherlands Institute for War Documentation
      </a>
      
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Srebrenica:_a_%E2%80%98safe%E2%80%99_area" title="Srebrenica: a safe area">
        Srebrenica: a safe area
       </a>
      </i>
      did not assign any blame to Haukland in regards to the massacre.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Claims_and_retraction_by_retired_NATO_SACLANT">
       Claims and retraction by retired NATO SACLANT
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: Claims and retraction by retired NATO SACLANT">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In March 2010,
      <a href="/wiki/John_J._Sheehan" title="John J. Sheehan">
       John Sheehan
      </a>
      , NATO's
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Allied_Commander_Atlantic" title="Supreme Allied Commander Atlantic">
       Supreme Allied Commander Atlantic
      </a>
      from 1994 to 1997, told a US Senate hearing that the Dutch had "declared a peace dividend and made a conscious effort to socialise their military  that includes the unionisation of their militaries, it includes open homosexuality", claiming that gay soldiers could result in events like Srebrenica.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317">
       <a href="#cite_note-317">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        317
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He claimed that his opinion was shared by the leadership of the Dutch armed forces, mentioning the name "Hankman Berman", who Sheehan added, had told him that the presence of gay soldiers at Srebrenica had sapped morale and contributed to the disaster.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318">
       <a href="#cite_note-318">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        318
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      General van den Breemen denied having said such a thing and called Sheehan's comments "total nonsense", Sheehan's remarks were also dismissed by the Dutch authorities as, "disgraceful" and "unworthy of anyone in the military".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319">
       <a href="#cite_note-319">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        319
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320">
       <a href="#cite_note-320">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        320
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321">
       <a href="#cite_note-321">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        321
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322">
       <a href="#cite_note-322">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        322
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323">
       <a href="#cite_note-323">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        323
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sheehan apologized to Dutch military officials on 29 March 2010, withdrawing his comments and blaming instead "the rules of engagement...developed by a political system with conflicting priorities and an ambivalent understanding of how to use the military."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324">
       <a href="#cite_note-324">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        324
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_the_1995_UN_Special_Representative_for_the_former_Yugoslavia">
       Criticism of the 1995 UN Special Representative for the former Yugoslavia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=86" title="Edit section: Criticism of the 1995 UN Special Representative for the former Yugoslavia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In Professor
      <a href="/wiki/Arne_Johan_Vetlesen" title="Arne Johan Vetlesen">
       Arne Johan Vetlesen
      </a>
      said "
      <a href="/wiki/Thorvald_Stoltenberg" title="Thorvald Stoltenberg">
       Thorvald Stoltenberg
      </a>
      's co-responsibility in Srebrenica boils down to that he through three years as a top broker contributed to create a climate - diplomatic, politic and indirectly militarily - such that
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mladic" title="Mladic">
       Mladic
      </a>
      calculated correctly when he figured that he could do exactly what he wanted with Srebrenica's Muslim population".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325">
       <a href="#cite_note-325">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        325
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">
       Aftenposten
      </a>
      said that
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica:_a_%27safe%27_area" title="Srebrenica: a 'safe' area">
        Srebrenica: a 'safe' area
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2002, criticises Stoltenberg, including the quote "... The appointment of Stoltenberg as a [peace] broker was unfortunate."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326">
       <a href="#cite_note-326">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        326
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Denial_and_scepticism">
       Denial and scepticism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=87" title="Edit section: Denial and scepticism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Srebrenica Genocide denial ranges from the refusal to acknowledge the judicial recognition of the killings as a crime of
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      to the denial of a massacre having taken place. The ICTY's finding of genocide, as affirmed by the ICJ, has been disputed on a variety of grounds, evidential and theoretical. The number of the dead has been questioned as has the nature of their deaths. It has been alleged that considerably fewer than 8,000 were killed and/or that most of those killed died in battle rather than by execution. It has been claimed that the interpretation of "genocide" is refuted by the survival of the women and children.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327">
       <a href="#cite_note-327">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        327
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Critics
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
         <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words.">
          who?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      cite a discrepancy between a figure of over 8,000 victims and the number of bodies found and identified as casting doubt on the explanation of the events, despite the long delays in locating mass graves and identifying the bodies in them.
     </p>
     <p>
      During the Bosnian war, Slobodan Miloevi had effective control of most Serbian media.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328">
       <a href="#cite_note-328">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        328
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329">
       <a href="#cite_note-329">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        329
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330">
       <a href="#cite_note-330">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        330
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331">
       <a href="#cite_note-331">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        331
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since the end of the war, scepticism about Srebrenica continues to be widespread among Serbs, Sonja Biserko, president of the Helsinki Committee for Human Rights in Serbia, and Edina Beirevi, the Faculty of Criminalistics, Criminology and Security Studies of the University of Sarajevo have pointed to a culture of denial of the Srebrenica genocide in Serbian society, taking many forms and present in particular in political discourse, the media, the law and the educational system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332">
       <a href="#cite_note-332">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        332
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 2005, Milo Milovanovi, a former commander of the Serb paramilitary unit
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Guard" title="Serbian Guard">
       Serbian Guard
      </a>
      who represents the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Democratic_Party_(Bosnia_and_Herzegovina)" title="Serbian Democratic Party (Bosnia and Herzegovina)">
       Serbian Democratic Party
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">
       Srebrenica
      </a>
      Municipal Assembly said that "the massacre is a lie; it is propaganda to paint a bad picture of the Serbian people. The Muslims are lying; they are manipulating the numbers; they are exaggerating what happened. Far more Serbs died at Srebrenica than Muslims."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333">
       <a href="#cite_note-333">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        333
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334">
       <a href="#cite_note-334">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        334
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Individuals_and_groups_who_have_challenged_or_denied_the_events_at_Srebrenica_as_genocide">
       Individuals and groups who have challenged or denied the events at Srebrenica as genocide
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_massacre&amp;action=edit&amp;section=88" title="Edit section: Individuals and groups who have challenged or denied the events at Srebrenica as genocide">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="782" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg/220px-Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg/330px-Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg/440px-Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Milorad_Dodik_mod.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Milorad_Dodik" title="Milorad Dodik">
         Milorad Dodik
        </a>
        , president of Republika Srpska, has repeatedly insisted that massacre cannot be labeled as genocide.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Milorad_Dodik" title="Milorad Dodik">
        Milorad Dodik
       </a>
       , President of Republika Srpska, stated in an interview with the Belgrade newspaper
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ve%C4%8Dernje_Novosti" title="Veernje Novosti">
        Veernje Novosti
       </a>
       in April 2010 that "we cannot and will never accept qualifying that event as a genocide". Dodik disowned the 2004 Republika Srpska report acknowledging the scale of the killing and apologising to the relatives of the victims, alleging that the report had been adopted because of pressure from the international community. Without substantiating the figure, he claimed that the number of victims was 3,500 rather than the 7,000 accepted by the report, alleging that 500 listed victims were alive and over 250 people buried in the Potocari memorial centre died elsewhere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335">
        <a href="#cite_note-335">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         335
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In July 2010, on the 15th anniversary of the massacre, Dodik declared that he did not regard the killings at Srebrenica as
       <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
        genocide
       </a>
       , and maintained that "If a genocide happened then it was committed against Serb people of this region where women, children and the elderly were killed en masse" (referring to eastern Bosnia).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Srebrenica_massacre_.27not_genocide.27_218-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Srebrenica_massacre_.27not_genocide.27-218">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         218
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In December 2010, Dodik condemned the
       <a href="/wiki/Peace_Implementation_Council" title="Peace Implementation Council">
        Peace Implementation Council
       </a>
       , an international community of 55 countries, for referring to the Srebrenica massacre as genocide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336">
        <a href="#cite_note-336">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         336
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tomislav_Nikoli%C4%87" title="Tomislav Nikoli">
        Tomislav Nikoli
       </a>
       , President of Serbia, stated on 2 June 2012 that "there was no genocide in Srebrenica. In Srebrenica, grave war crimes were committed by some Serbs who should be found, prosecuted and punished. [] It is very difficult to indict someone and prove before a court that an event qualifies as genocide."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_337-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guardian-337">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         337
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        La Nation
       </i>
       , a bi-monthly Swiss newspaper, published a series of articles claiming that 2,000 soldiers were killed in the "pseudo-massacre" in Srebrenica. The
       <a href="/wiki/Society_for_Threatened_Peoples" title="Society for Threatened Peoples">
        Society for Threatened Peoples
       </a>
       and Swiss Association Against Impunity filed a joint suit against
       <i>
        La Nation
       </i>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Genocide_denial" title="Genocide denial">
        genocide denial
       </a>
       . Swiss law prohibits genocide denial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap_224-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ap-224">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         224
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Phillip Corwin, former UN Civilian Affairs Coordinator in Bosnia, advisor and contributor to the work of the Srebrenica Research Group
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-srebrenica-report.com_338-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-srebrenica-report.com-338">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         338
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       said "What happened in Srebrenica was not a single large massacre of Muslims by Serbs, but rather a series of very bloody attacks and counterattacks over a three-year period."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339">
        <a href="#cite_note-339">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         339
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Lewis_MacKenzie" title="Lewis MacKenzie">
        Lewis MacKenzie
       </a>
       , former commander of the United Nations Protection Force (UNPROFOR) in Bosnia, was continuing to challenge the description of genocide in 2009 on the grounds firstly that the number of men and boys killed had been exaggerated by a factor of 4 and secondly that transfer of the women and children by bus contradicted the notion of genocide  the women would have been killed first if there had been an intent to destroy the group. Writing in the Journal of Military and Strategic Studies (Vol. 12, Issue 1, Fall 2009), MacKenzie expressed his opinion without reference to the detailed arguments published by the ICTY Trial and Appeal Chambers in the Krstic case judgements published several years earlier and confirmed by the ICJ since.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340">
        <a href="#cite_note-340">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         340
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341">
        <a href="#cite_note-341">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         341
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_Research_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Srebrenica Research Group (page does not exist)">
        Srebrenica Research Group
       </a>
       , led by
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_S._Herman" title="Edward S. Herman">
        Edward S. Herman
       </a>
       , Professor Emeritus of Finance at the
       <a href="/wiki/Wharton_School_of_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania">
        Wharton School of the University of Pennsylvania
       </a>
       , describes itself as a self-financed group of journalists and academic researchers who have reviewed the evidence relating to the capture of Srebrenica and compared the facts with the public portrayal of events. Members of the Group include journalist and publicist Jonathan Rooper, journalist
       <a href="/wiki/George_Szamuely" title="George Szamuely">
        George Szamuely
       </a>
       , the writer and film-director George Bogdanich,
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Mandel_(law_professor)" title="Michael Mandel (law professor)">
        Michael Mandel
       </a>
       , Professor of International Law at York University in Toronto, the commentator on media coverage of conflict Dr. Philip Hammond of London South Bank University, the researcher and archivist Tim Fenton, the foreign policy writer David Peterson and Dr Milan Bulajic, former head of the Yugoslav State Commission on War Crimes. Advisors and collaborators include Phillip Corwin, former UN Civilian Affairs Coordinator in Bosnia, Carlos Martins Branco, Deputy Director of the UN monitoring organisation in Bosnia, UNMO,
       <a href="/wiki/Diana_Johnstone" title="Diana Johnstone">
        Diana Johnstone
       </a>
       , author of
       <i>
        Fool's Crusade: Yugoslavia NATO and Western Delusions
       </i>
       , Professor Vera Vratusa, the researcher George Pumphrey, the author Milivoje Ivanisevic, the military forensic specialist Dr.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoran_Stankovic" title="Zoran Stankovic">
        Zoran Stankovic
       </a>
       , and the forensic archeologist Dr. Srboljub Zivanovic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342">
        <a href="#cite_note-342">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         342
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px">
        <div class="thumbimage">

          <img alt="" data-file-height="2074" data-file-width="1481" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg/120px-Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg/180px-Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg/240px-Yehuda_Bauer_1.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:242px;max-width:242px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Efraim_Zuroff_(May_2007).jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="3344" data-file-width="4725" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg/240px-Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg/360px-Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg/480px-Efraim_Zuroff_%28May_2007%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="clear:left">
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
        The description of Srebrenica as a genocidal massacre has been disputed by
        <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
         Holocaust
        </a>
        scholar
        <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">
         Yehuda Bauer
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         left
        </i>
        ), and the director of the
        <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">
         Simon Wiesenthal Center
        </a>
        office in
        <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">
         Jerusalem
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Efraim_Zuroff" title="Efraim Zuroff">
         Efraim Zuroff
        </a>
        (
        <i>
         right
        </i>
        )
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2015:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Israeli
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       scholar
       <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">
        Yehuda Bauer
       </a>
       described Srebrenica as "an act of mass murder, not a genocide" and stated that he could see no evidence that Serb forces intended, in whole or in part, to exterminate the Bosniaks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343">
        <a href="#cite_note-343">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         343
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The director of the
       <a href="/wiki/Simon_Wiesenthal_Center" title="Simon Wiesenthal Center">
        Simon Wiesenthal Center
       </a>
       office in Israel,
       <a href="/wiki/Efraim_Zuroff" title="Efraim Zuroff">
        Efraim Zuroff
       </a>
       , also disagrees that Serb forces had genocidal intent. He explained: "As far as I know, what happened [in Srebrenica] does not [fit] the description or the definition of genocide. I think the decision to call it genocide was made for political reasons. Obviously a tragedy occurred, innocent people lost their lives and their memory should be preserved." Zuroff also called attempts to equate Srebrenica to the Holocaust "horrible" and "absurd", saying: "I wish the Nazis moved aside Jewish women and children before their bloody rampage, instead of murdering them, but that, as we know, did not happen."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344">
        <a href="#cite_note-344">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         344
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>

         The Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina  Mitrovic and others (Kravice)  Accused of the criminal offence of genocide in violation of Article 171 of the Criminal Code of Bosnia and Herzegovina (
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.sudbih.gov.ba/?opcija=predmeti&amp;id=22&amp;jezik=e" rel="nofollow">
          X-KR-05/24  Mitrovic and others (Kravice)
         </a>
         ).
        </span>
       </li>

       <li id="cite_note-327">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-327">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Alternative Views
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.srebrenica-report.com/" rel="nofollow">
            Report
           </a>
           of
           <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Srebrenica_Research_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Srebrenica Research Group (page does not exist)">
            Srebrenica Research Group
           </a>
           , alleged that "the contention that as many as 8,000 Muslims were killed has no basis in available evidence and is essentially a political construct".
          </span>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://128.121.186.47/ISSA/reports/Balkan/Sep1903.htm" rel="nofollow">
            Report of
            <i>
             International Strategic Studies Association
            </i>
            (ISSA)
           </a>
           , claimed that the "alleged casualty number of 7,000 victims [is] vastly inflated and unsupported by evidence"
          </span>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.mail-archive.com/serbian_way@antic.org/msg00008.html" rel="nofollow">
            The real story behind Srebrenica
           </a>
           by the former UNPROFOR commander, Gen. Lewis MacKenzie,
           <i>
            The Globe and Mail
           </i>
           , 14 July 2005.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.slobodan-milosevic.org/news/smorg-sreb101604.htm" rel="nofollow">
            "The Forbidden Srebrenica report"
           </a>
           , report denying the Srebrenica massacre issued by the Republika Srpska Bureau for Cooperation with the ICTY in September 2002.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.zmag.org/content/showarticle.cfm?ItemID=8244" rel="nofollow">
            The Politics of the Srebrenica Massacre
           </a>
           article argues that only some Bosniaks were executed, most died in battle, and some of the bodies in mass graves are actually Serbs, by Edward S. Herman, 7 July 2005
          </span>
         </li>
        </ul>
